電影專刊

日本蒲田攝影塲參觀記 289

— 東林

四年前一天早晨的所見

我在從前發表的「日本的電影屑談」内，曾經說過，這蒲田攝影塲就是松竹映畫株式會社專門攝取現代片的場所。在日本牠是歷史最長，並且成績最佳的現代片攝影塲。

這是四年前的一個夏天的上午吧，當時我還住在東京郊外的　大森，得到蒲田攝影塲開放的消息，連忙搭了高架電車到蒲田去。從大森到蒲田只有一站路程，所以不到五分鐘，已經達到了目的地。走出蒲田車决，朝北走去，再轉了一個灣，遠遠地就看見，圍着紅白布的攝影塲了。

買了一張門票，我就向着一間大房子的内跑進去，只見有許多長桌，上面陳列着無數的建築物和車輛的模型。我問站在旁邊的招待員，這是做甚麽用的？他對我說，這就是銀幕中所映出來的各種房屋和大厦，火災的一幕，就是燒這種模型的。我聽了他的話，半信半疑地離開了。

走出了這大房子的後門，正要往前走的時候，不料頭上的帽子吹得一丈多遠。我不能不驚疑了：；怎麽好好地天氣，有這麽大的風呢？我拾了帽了，好奇心引我走過去看，究竟什麽東西在那裏作怪。轉灣一看，我明白了；原來這風就是從一架高而大的，形似風扇般的怪東西外發出來的。旁邊站着的工程師，正在那裏對觀衆解說着，這機器就是製造狂風用的。

離開了羣衆，我又轉了一個灣，看見一間小小的車站；站内有一張木板製成的火車的正面，裝着停車的樣子。我想這就是所謂電影中的火車吧！走不到幾步，前面有一個小池，四面的花草，培植得和花園一樣。只有幾步的距離，就有一間車站和花園，這種景象除了攝影塲以外是不能夠看到的。

前面有許多人圍着，我亦走上去，擠進了人羣，看個明白。原來是在攝取下雨的光景。說起這雨眞是可笑極了，這不過是站在高處的人，所撥下來的水吧了！一個演員，亦没有撑着傘，被這水撥得像「河水鬼」一樣的戰慓着·我不覺想起做電影演員的困苦。

這樣東張西望時間不覺已是中午了，我肚子很餓，就出去吃午飯去了。

影片談評

評「桃花村」ＨappyＥevnＡlter 290

— 凌鶴

在「ＴellＭeＴoＮight」（春江花月夜）之後又有了這一部同一情調的「Ｈ「appyＥverＡfler」，當然，這不是偶然的，我們在這中間多少可以找得出製片家的用意。前一部的内容如何，反正聰明的觀家都會知道，似乎用不着在這裏解剖，那末「桃花村」中又告訴了我們一些什麽呢？它譏笑了好萊塢的製片商，揭穿了少女們對於黄金電影的幻想。然而這都不是本片的製作者主要的任務，它最重大的目的在於敎觀衆們在美麗的畫面之前逃避現實，爲了愛情的美滿而退避到世外桃源中去。很顯然的，在現實社會中，樂享田園的生活早已給現實的經濟組織毁滅無遺，而我們也不再是太平盛世的順民，我們日以繼夜的掙扎着，我們還有「回到桃花村去度那安閒生活」的可能嗎？然而本片作者的用意也就在這裏，他敎我們在幻想中繼續幻想下去。

正如上面所述，爲了要使觀衆沉醉於美麗的幻境，必須要有美麗的畫面，於是導演者便得使用純熟的技巧，載歌載舞的使本片充滿了浪漫的情調，再加上精緻的攝影，增加着那種醉人的色素，於是他的使命乃得成功。

然而導演對於少數的場面仍然是不大活潑的，最顯著的是一個麗琳哈蕙在中間，每邊一個男性並排的而且重覆，好幾個鏡頭，這在畫面上未免是過於機械。其次導演在情調上也還不夠柔和，假如以「柔和」成爲本片之精髓的話。

小范朋克 291

— 福倫

將有中華之遊

小范朋克自與其妻瓊克勞馥離異之後，忽又被人控告誘惑罪。范正從　於法律解决。（俟此案了結，即將束裝西遊，屆時當與其父范朋克相會於滬，然後同赴各地遊獵。自計大槪須俟秋凉之後，以訟案尙須延梗時日也。再則小范朋友自與瓊克勞馥宣告分居之後，仍時相過往。據范自言情感反較以前密切，已相偕同出四次，實較與任何女性同遊爲樂云。至於離婚一節，彼與瓊俱不願立卽提出討論，因雙力均無意於娶嫁。而小范朋克則立誓必俟功成業就之時，始再言娶云。

同時劇中没有顯明的高潮，一點也没有力的刺激，雖然劇中也許並不需要這些，可是因此便不能給觀衆何等印象，就導演來說，乃　找不出何等特色的。

演員方面，誰也没有驚人的成績，都是懶懶的平平過去。女主角麗琳哈蕙ＬilianＨarey在夢中的場面和當着美國製片家面前表演跳舞的塲面，都使我們回想起她過去成績，其他方面也總算得存了那種活潑的態度。賈克霍爾伯ＪackＨulbert和遜尼海爾ＳonnieＨale在本片中都不見何等精采，但亦很少胡閙的場合。

收音是好的，佈景亦佳。然而最好的還是攝影方面。然而無論如何，即就技巧說，確是一部堪當上遭的片子。

（觀衆意見「脂粉市場」的觀感） 292

— 史澤永

明星公司繼「自由之花」以後，四達通有聲影片的「脂粉市場」，十四日起，在新光大戲院公映了！乍看這四個字的名命，我們覺得這萬惡的社會，帶了很濃厚脂粉色彩的上海，便可以知道女子在社會上的地位，不過如這般而已！

二十世紀的上海，一般女子的職業，根本就没有穩固的地位；伊們雖然天天在高喊着婦女解放，自由，提高，可是，那一個有澈底了解的？雖意志堅决如李翠芬，也不免被資本家所侮辱和玩弄。何况有些女子，還自甘墮落的呢？

在這裏，在下並不是有意得罪現代的女性；的確，伊們的意志，是太薄弱了！並且一些也不了解現代社會的虛僞。伊們只憑了一時的意氣，似「飛蛾撲火，」只向着有光的地方亂衝，忘見了前途之危險，要從黑暗的社會中，去尋求光明的出路，要耐勞吃苦，才有好的結果。否則没有這們容易的事哩！

觀「脂粉市塲」後幾點感想 293

— 梅邨

「脂粉市塲」確是一張意識較好的影片，牠暴露了社會上的惡勢力和男女間的黑暗，使我觀後覺得滿意下面就是我觀後的幾點感想：

一，百貨公司的四周，旣没有電車和汽車，連黄包車也只一二輛，來往行人也寥若晨星，我以爲旣稱百貨公司，應設在像永安先施那麽樣熱鬧的塲合，纔可以適合大公司的繁華·

二，公司内部的塲面，也應裝得熱鬧一點，像電梯内只有進的而没有出的，並且只有四五個，似嫌清淡·

三，顧客在脂粉部買東西，與女店員胡調，女店員却和他們做眉眼，也嫌失當，這一點我想觀衆都以爲不滿的，在我旁坐的幾位朋友，都在說「簡直没有這樣事實」。

四，飾李翠芬的胡蝶面部表情甚佳，尤其在默思的當兒，眼瞳一瞬，頓現緊漲，心事盡露。如果當時引用别人的聲調來說明她的意思，那末更覺　有力了。

五，末幾幕指示奮鬥的結果，由揀茶葉以至接電話開小商店，其中幾段生活的介紹很簡明，是導演的聰明處。

「脂粉市塲」我評 294

— 許瓊

戀愛的穿揷毫無理由

婦女職業，在目前我們中國，的確是一個嚴重的問題。並不是苛刻的說：一般的公司銀行商店，招請女職員，美其名曰提倡婦女職業，其實呢？不過爲招徠一般，急色兒而已，於是來了許多侮辱女性的雅號：什麽花瓶啦，屛風啦，活招牌啦，本能地告訴我們：婦女職業在中國不過玩玩而已。不騷不媚招徠不了主顧，不會向上司獻殷勤，保不住飯碗。這是婦女職業的金科玉律。「脂粉市塲」抓住了這個現實的婦女問題來加一暴露，雖然是很適當的；但我們認爲暴露得不夠，更没有理由的安放了一個歪曲的戀愛故事，動搖了全劇的本身，糢糊了觀衆的心靈！

在結尾，太冲滿了Ｒomantio，因爲從做工所鬥爭出來，並不會這樣的迅速而成功了老閬娘，所謂認識社會的缺點，也根本没有認識。

至於表情：太矯揉造作，女職員哼哼唱歌是有的，在櫃檯裏跳舞太過份些；經理少爺的抹眼睛看女職員太過於做作；胡蝶幾個哭的塲面很好；王獻齋是成功的。

電影小說千古恨（ＴheＷhiteＳister）（二） 295

— 思蘋

米高梅出品海倫海絲主演

爲愛情而犧牲名譽和幸福

恩納斯篤又重新攀談起來了，但是斗的又來一個波折。一輛破舊小車在人叢中轉轉灣灣的行駛猛力撞在親王車子的後身。安琪拉緊張地向着後窗外面張望，她的父親和車夫踅去調查車子撞損到怎麽樣子。

從這輛破舊小車裏走出來的人穿着一身軍裝！一個軍人，安琪拉想着這人生得漂亮。這人瞥見她好奇似的觀望，便跑到車旁。

「早安，」他面帶風流的笑容開口說。但是恩納斯篤一見這個神情便馬上把窗帷拉下。「無恥！」他發着貴族的脾氣咕嚕着。這車子便開動了。

「那是誰？」這少年軍人跑回到他的車子時問那些嘲笑着同伴。

「那，居望尼，是謝樂孟德老親王，」一個人說。「那美麗的公主就是他的女兒。」

居望尼如獲珍寳似的拍拍他的破舊車子的發動機。他的心早已飄飄蕩蕩地跟着那華麗的車子所載去的媚笑的倩影去了。

在謝樂孟德王宮裏，恩納斯篤拘守着細節親吻安琪拉的手，便笑着說要趕火車到羅馬去了。安琪拉踅到對向市鎭的窗前，幽恩默想地傾斜出身子向外看。

「他們眞開心呀，密娜，」她說。「聽那音樂！」她輕微提起她的裙子試一回舞步。

「密娜，我又夢想他了，」他紅暈着說。

「他是誰呢？」密娜做着針綫反問。

「那人我夢想的。這次他的名字是渥郎社。他騎着有黑斑的白馬。母親也同在那裏。她是很美麗！金黄色的頭髮。母親有没有金黄色的頭髮呢？爲怎麽没有母親的照片呢？」

這不是一個新問題，但是密娜回答：

「我告訴過您了丨因爲您的父親不願意它呀。」安琪拉回到陽台，側身靠上欄桿凝神眺望。

「密娜，」她突然說，「我們出去！我們吃飯是不是還有兩點鏡？去看看嘉年會！」安琪拉說着兜進房間。抓住她的披肩。「我一個人去，」他反抗着說了就飛奔而去。密娜說聲「您不能呀！」便一把抓起他的外套趕着追去。

貼近着嘉年會看眞熱鬧！她的芳心卜卜地跳。農人與兵混合着，跳舞，玩，前列遊行隊裏有稗官野史的人物，有巨人，有兩三個人裝成的怪獸。一匹馬伸着鼻子對着快樂到極點的安琪拉嗅，一忽兒又跌倒在地，反翻打滾。在這當兒，前次破舊小車裏的軍人在人叢中出現，站在他們面前，微傴着身。

「公主午安，」居望尼說。這次可没有嚴厲的手在他和那嫵媚的漲紅的面龐之間拉下帷幕了。

1933.05.18

The Enemy Advances Towards Hsükochuang 1

Ho Chu-kuo's Troops Gather West of Tangku

Enemy Cavalry Active Near Yutien

Japanese Planes Bomb Ningho 2

Lutai, Tsunhua, and Fengrun Front Lines All Change, Tangshan Threatened, Wan and Ho Wang's Armies Ordered to Withdraw and Defend the West Bank of the Chi Canal, Transferred on the 16th Night, Expected to Completely Arrive for Defense by the 17th Night. On the 16th Night at 8 PM in Tangshan City, Traitorous Elements Disrupted Station Order, Plotting Rebellion, Telegraph and Telephone Communications Were Briefly Cut, After My Armored Vehicles Collaborated with Sentries, Armed Suppression, No Incident Occurred, Guarding on the 17th, North-Ning Trains Suspended to Tangshan Starting the 17th. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) The Vanguard of the Japanese Army on the North-Ning Line is Advancing Towards Tangshan Today, First Sending Sentries to Reconnoiter Near Tangshan. My Armored Vehicle □□ No. Left Hsükochuang at 8 AM This Morning, Stationed at the Station, Guarding. There is Still a Small Number of My Cavalry on Both Sides of the Railway, Undertaking Protection Work. Wan Fu-lin Left Lutai Station Yesterday at 3 PM by More Than Ten Cars Along with Key Members of the Army Corps, Went to □□ to Recover Dispersed Troops. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) The Military Affairs Committee Orders Ho Chu-kuo and Yang Cheng-hao's Armies to Firmly Defend the □□ Line with All Their Strength. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Two Japanese Planes Reconnoitered Ningho, Yutien, and the Lutai Hsükochuang Area on the North-Ning Line at 8 AM This Morning, Dropping Four Heavy Bombs in Ningho. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Ho Chu-kuo's Troops are Gathering West of Tangku, Relocating to Chünliangcheng for Deployment. Sung Che-yuan's Troops are Arranging Defensive Works in the Shihmen Area. At the Shali River Between Fengrun and Yutien, My Covering Force of About Two Companies Was Fiercely Attacked by the Enemy's Vanguard Cavalry and Bombed by Enemy Planes. Only Forty-Two Survived. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Paoti Dispatch, Most of My □ Army Has Reached the Pre-Determined Front Line East of the Paochi Road, and is Currently Arranging Defenses. Near Yutien, a Unit of the □ Division is Still Defending. The Enemy's Vanguard Cavalry is Currently Active Between Shahopu and Liangchiatien East of Yutien, Showing No Immediate Rush. The Enemy Arriving Near Fengrun Consists of the Takada and Matsuda Brigades of the Japanese 6th Division and the Ushiga Brigade of the 14th Regiment. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) My Army on the North-Ning Line Has Withdrawn West of Tangku. Order Along the Route is Extremely Disrupted. Ho Chu-kuo Has Arrived at Lutai From Hsükochuang, and Wan Fu-lin Has Arrived at Yangtsun From Lutai, Separately Gathering Their Troops. Their Covering Troops are Still Between Hsükochuang and Lutai. North-Ning Trains Currently Only Run to Tangku, Because There are Too Many Troop Trains Going East, Order is Chaotic, and Pro-Japanese Traitors are Active Along the Route. Bombs are Occasionally Found Beside the Tracks, Making Travel Inconvenient. After the Loss of Fengrun on the Pingyu Highway, the Enemy Continues to Advance. The Situation in Yutien is Currently Unclear. Wang I-che's and Other Armies are All Between Yutien and Paoti. On That Road, He Li-chung, Weng Chao-yuan, and Shen Ke's Divisions are Fighting Hard. There are Rumors of Weng Being Injured and He Being Almost Captured, Still Awaiting Confirmation. (10th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Since the Fighting in Luanhsi and Kupeikou Became Intense, the Situation in Peiping and Tientsin Has Become Tense. Chiang Recently Telegraphed Peiping, With Earnest Instructions on the Issue of the Security of North China. Also, the Enemy Intends to Occupy Miyun, Tangshan, Fengrun, and Tsunhua, Place My Peiping and Tientsin Under Siege, Then Temporarily Halt the Advance, and Force Me into a Treaty Under Duress. However, Miyun is Still in the Hands of My Army. It is Heard That the Japanese Side Greatly Desires to Establish Neutral Zones on the Miyun, Tsunhua, Tangshan, and Fengrun Lines, and Encourages Britain and the United States to Come Forward to Participate in the Movement to Demarcate Neutral Zones. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) After My Army Withdrew From Tangshan Last Night, the Enemy's Plainclothes Troops and Defeated Soldiers and Bandits Harassed the Area That Evening. The Businesses North of the Railway Were Robbed Clean. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Chihsien Dispatch, Around Lungching Pass, My □ Army Transferred Positions on the Evening of the 15th Due to the Enemy's Threat on the Right Flank. The Majority Has Retreated to the Line East of Chihsien □□, and Made Contact With the □ Army. Fortifications Have Been Constructed Through the Night. The Enemy Attacking in That Direction is the Hattori 14th Mixed Brigade, and the Nakamura Brigade of the 10th Division. (17th Dispatch)

(Tientsin) Foreign News, The Puppet Army of Li Chi-chun's Unit of Over 3,000 Troops Entered Tangshan City at Noon on the 17th. The Vanguard Team Has Set Out Towards Hsükochuang. Enemy Traces Were Discovered Five or Six Li Outside Tangfang at Noon on the 17th. My Armored Train is Stationed at Hsükochuang and Tangfang Stations. Between Lutai and Tangku, My Army and the Enemy Intend to Not Stop Advancing. The Situation in That Direction is Extremely Tense. The Japanese Army Unit Stationed in Tientsin Also Denies That the Japanese Army is Withdrawing Outside the Great Wall. (17th Dispatch)

Entire Two Battalions of Wan's Troops Sacrificed 3

(Peiping) Wan's Battalion Commanders Liu Run-chuan and Chao Shao-tsung Led Their Troops From the Night of the 15th, Along the Line of Tsochiawu and Tuanshanzi on the Pingyu Highway, and Engaged in Fierce Fighting with the Enemy for a Day and a Night. On the Evening of the 17th, All the Soldiers of My Two Battalions Were Sacrificed. Both Battalion Commanders Were Injured. My Army Withdrew to a New Front Line. The Injured Battalion Commanders Will Be Transported to Peiping Today and Sent to Tungren Hospital for Treatment. (17th Dispatch)

Enemy Cavalry Advances Towards Hsükochuang 4

(Peiping) Chünliangcheng Dispatch, Yesterday Afternoon, Three Enemy Planes Reconnoitered Over Tangshan for a Long Time, Dropping Eleven Bombs. After 10 PM, A Unit of the Enemy's Cavalry Advanced to Tangshan. Three Columns of Enemy Armored Trains Guarded Tangshan. After 3 AM This Morning, The Main Force of the Enemy Fully Entered Tangshan, Forcing Merchants and Residents to Hang Japanese and Puppet Flags, and Posting Slogans Throughout the City. At 5 AM This Morning, The Enemy Cavalry Further Advanced Towards Hsükochuang. There Was No Fighting Along the Way. The North-Ning Road Defense Line Will Be Defended by the First Army in Tangku, Blocking the Enemy's Advance. (17th Dispatch)

Sung, Wang, and Other Armies Complete Deployment 5

(Peiping) Sung Che-yuan, Wang I-che, and Other Armies are Defending Along the Area East of Chihsien and Paoti, North to Huangyakuan, and Connecting with My Army South of Shihhsia, South to Tungfengningho East, Coordinating with My Army in Lutai. Currently, Deployment Has Been Completed. (17th Dispatch)

Main Japanese Force Near Kaiping 6

(Tientsin) According to News From Tangshan This Morning, Last Night the Chinese Army Abandoned Kaiping and Tangshan. The Main Japanese Force is Still Near Kaiping. "Manchukuo" Sentry Teams Have Approached Tangshan and Will Occupy the Town Sooner or Later. During the Recent Battles, the Assets of the Kaiping Mining Company Were Not Damaged, and No Employees Were Injured. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Tientsin) This Morning's Tangshan Telegram States That Two to Three Thousand "Manchukuo" Troops Under the Command of Li Chi-chun Have Advanced to the Vicinity of Kuyeh, Ten Miles East of Kaiping, This Morning. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

Standing Committee Meeting of Military Affairs Committee Suspended Yesterday 7

(Peiping) The Standing Committee Meeting of the Military Affairs Committee Has Been Suspended Today Due to No Special Cases. (17th Dispatch)

Enemy Troops Have Not Yet Crossed the Tou River 8

(Peiping) Military News, Near Hsükochuang, There are Still My Armored Vehicles and Cavalry □ Units, Currently Constructing Fortifications in the □□ Area, Preparing to Firmly Defend. The Enemy Facing Them Has Not Yet Crossed the Tou River. Most of the Enemy in That Direction Consists of Puppet Troops and a Unit of the Japanese Army. (17th Dispatch)

North-Ning Locomotive Materials Transported to Loyang 9

(Peiping) The Tangshan Repair Factory of the North-Ning Road, Upon Order of the Ministry of Railways, Is Transporting All Unfinished Locomotives and Carriages, Wheels, etc. Stored in the Factory to Loyang. This Morning, Several Freight Trains, Separately Carrying the Engine and Parts, Transferred Through Fengtai to Changhsintien, Directly Transporting to Loyang. (17th Dispatch)

Enemy Cavalry Discovered West of Tangshan Suburbs 10

Lutai, The Enemy Entered Tangshan From Fengrun. This Afternoon, Forty-Some Enemy Cavalry Were Discovered in the Western Suburbs of Tangshan City, Without Advancing West. My "Henan" Armored Vehicle is Still Guarding Tangshan Station. The North-Ning Telephone is Still Connected to Tangshan Station. The Tangshan City Telegraph Bureau, Being Under Surveillance, is No Longer Sending Reports. (17th Dispatch)

My Main Force Concentrates Towards Chihsien 11

(Peiping) In Terms of the Situation in Tsunhua, it Has Become a Bulge. Strategically Speaking, a Withdrawal is Necessary. The Area is Still Covered by My Army's Covering Troops, Confronting the Enemy. The Main Force Has Concentrated Towards Chihsien. (17th Dispatch)

Miyun Front Silent

My Army Still Guards the Nanshankou Area 12

(Peiping) No Fierce Fighting in Miyun Today. I Still Guard the Defense Area Around Mount Chiusong. The Rumor of a Position Shift is Inaccurate. Hsü Ting-yao is Personally Commanding at the Front. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Miyun Dispatch, The Front-Line Fighting Has Gradually Subsided Yesterday and Today. The Enemy is Constructing Fortifications and Deploying Artillery Positions on the Line East of Shihhsia, Seeming to Be Preparing to Attack. My Army's Foremost Line Still Guards the Nanshankou Area About Sixty Miles North of Miyun, Constructing Solid Fortifications Between □□. The Enemy in That Direction Consists of the Entire Japanese 8th Division, and a Unit of the 16th Division and Several Thousand Puppet Manchukuo Troops. (17th Dispatch)

Enemy Planes Reconnoitered Miyun Yesterday 13

(Peiping) Miyun Dispatch, At 8 AM This Morning, An Enemy Plane Flew Over Miyun for Over Ten Minutes of Reconnaissance, Flying North, Without Dropping Bombs. (17th Dispatch)

Enemy Stealthily Attacks Huanggangyu Position 14

(Peiping) Miyun Dispatch, The Enemy Facing Mount Chiusong Constantly Shelled My Army From the Hsiao Hsinkailing Area Yesterday, and Used Searchlights to Probe My Positions. After 10 PM Last Night, Enemy Sentries Stealthily Attacked My Huanggangyu Position and Were Repelled. At Lutouchuang on the Right Flank, My Kuan Division is Still Continuing to Fiercely Fight the Enemy on the High Ground. The Enemy Has Consistently Failed. Today, The Enemy Again Used Over Ten Tanks to Attack My Lutouchuang Position, and Engaged in Hand-to-Hand Combat With My Army for a Long Time. My Kuan Division Dispatched Another Brave Unit, to Circumvent the Rear of the Tanks in a Certain Area, Attempting to Cut Off the Enemy's Retreat. Because the Enemy Discovered This, My Army Suffered Many Casualties. (17th Dispatch)

Enemy Planes Bomb Hsiao's Division's Position 15

(Peiping) Hsiao Chih-chu's 16th Dispatch States That Formations of Five or Six Enemy Planes, Two Heavy Bombers, Reconnoitered the Entire Front Line and Rear of My Position at Low Altitude All Day. The Most Bombs Fell in Chiusongshan Village and Mujayu, Wounding Two Soldiers and Civilians and Several Civilian Houses. My Army Suffered Slight Damage. Most of the Enemy is Now in Shihhsia. The Enemy and My Sentries are Very Close, and There Have Been Small Contacts From Time to Time. This Afternoon, Ten-Some Enemy Cavalry Carried Out an Attack in Force on My Position and Were Repelled by My Plainclothes Sentries. (17th Dispatch)

Huang Chieh Left Peiping to Return to Defense Yesterday 16

(Peiping) Huang Chieh Left Peiping at 6 PM Today With Chief of Staff Shih Hung-lieh, Returning to Defense. Before Departure, at 9 AM, Upon Invitation From Mei I-chi, He Went to Tsinghua University to Give a Lecture on the History of the Anti-Japanese War at Nantienmen. The Speech Was Extremely Passionate and Lasted Two Hours. The Audience Was Deeply Moved. (17th Dispatch)

Huang Fu and His Party Arrive in Peiping 17

When the Special Train Arrived at Tientsin Station

Someone Threw a Bomb and Missed

Denying the Talk of Sino-Japanese Compromise 18

(Tientsin) Huang Fu's Special Train Arrived in Tientsin at 9:40 AM on the 17th. He Disembarked at the New Station. Tzu Hsüeh-chung and Leaders of Provincial and Municipal Organizations All Came to the Station to Welcome Him. The Station Interior and Exterior, and the Tachin Road Were Under Extremely Tight Security. Police and Military Police Were Fully Armed on Duty. Huang Went to the Provincial Government to Rest. A Luncheon Was Held to Welcome Him. In Addition to Various Provincial Committee Members, Wang I-tang and Chien Tsung-tse Were Among Those Present. They Discussed the Current Situation for a Long Time. He Left Tientsin at 1:40 PM in the Afternoon to Go to Peiping. Huang Answered Reporters' Questions as Follows: (1) I Am Coming North This Time Under the Central Government's Intentions, and Will Naturally Follow the Central Government's Intentions. I Believe That if All Parties Can Be Organized, Step by Step, in Harmony and Cooperation, Public Morale Can Be Stabilized. Party, Government, and Military Authorities, as Well as the General Public, Should Also Share the Heavy Burden of the Current Situation, National Crisis, and Work Together. Otherwise, Everyone Will Go Their Own Way and Go Against Each Other, and There Will Be No Certainty About Anything. (2) Resisting While Negotiating, President Wang Has Repeatedly Said This. The Entire Issue Still Awaits the Leadership of the Central Government. But After Arriving in Peiping, if Necessary, I Will Briefly Confer With All Parties. (3) The Rumor of Compromise is Just That. The Central Government Has Not Said This. The Situation in North China is So Dire. How Can There Be Compromise? Who Dares to Talk About Compromise? (4) The Military Organs in Peiping and Tientsin Moving to Other Places and Turning Peiping and Tientsin Into a Buffer Zone is Entirely Unheard Of. This Must Be Villainous Rumors. (5) The Affairs of North China Are Very Complicated. After Arriving in Peiping, I Will Confer At Length With the Various Committee Members. Moreover, This Type of Organization is Newly Established. How To Proceed Still Needs Joint Research. As For the Matters That Should Be Handled, Even if the Organs Are Not Established, They Must Be Handled First. Committee Member Ho Will Be Responsible For Military Affairs, and I Can Also Assist in the Process. When Huang's Special Train Had Just Entered the Platform, Outside the East Yang Banner, Someone Suddenly Threw a Bomb. Six Soldiers and Police Guarding the Bridge Were Simultaneously Stunned. The No. 21 Bridge Foundation Was Destroyed. The Bridge Was Slightly Damaged. The Criminal Suffered Minor Injuries to His Hands, Feet, and Face, Was Arrested on the Spot, Sent to the First Army Headquarters, and Confessed to Being Liu Kuei-sheng, 16 Years Old, From Tsaochou, Shantung, Working at Liu San-fen's Fertilizer Factory in Chenchiakou. He Firmly Denied Throwing the Bomb. He Was Tied and Beheaded Outside the New Station This Afternoon as a Warning. Also, Half an Hour Before Huang Left Tientsin, a Bomb Was Discovered on Tachin Road, Huangwei Road, and the Tsancha on Tan Chia Bridge. Considering Its Intention, it Seemed to Plot to Bomb Huang's Car. Fortunately, It Was Discovered Early and No Incident Occurred. Two Suspects Were Arrested on the Spot. According to General Speculation, the Atmosphere of Compromise With Japan Has Been Strong in Recent Days, Inciting the Anger of Patriotic Elements, Using the Bomb as a Warning to Huang. This Theory Seems Quite Plausible. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Huang Fu, Along With Ho Chi-kung, Tao Lü-chien, and More Than Ten Others, Arrived in Peiping at 4:40 PM This Afternoon. Liu Chung-chieh, Chiang Po-cheng, Chang Chün, Wang Shu-chang, Chou Ta-wen, and Others All Came to the Station to Welcome Him. The Military Affairs Committee Dispatched a Company of Guards and a Platoon of Central Military Police, Stationing Them Around the Station. After Leaving the Station, Huang Went to Chüjen Hall to Visit Ho Ying-chin. They Spoke for Over an Hour. He Returned to Fengtse Garden in Nanhai to Rest. Huang Said That the Political Affairs Committee Has Not Yet Determined the Date of Establishment Because the Committee Members Have Not Yet Arrived. However, Committee Affairs Can Be Contacted and Handled With the Various Committee Members at Any Time. To Cope With the Crisis in North China, We Must Adhere to the Central Government's Consistent Policy of Negotiating While Resisting. All Parties Must Work Together to Succeed. The Rumor of Sino-Japanese Compromise is Absolutely Inaccurate. I Will First Inspect the Situation and Then Determine the Method for Reorganizing North China's Political Affairs. Ho Will Be Responsible For Military Affairs. The Central Government Still Intends to Take Charge of Everything in North China. As For Stabilizing the Public Morale in North China, There is No Certainty. The Rumor That Peiping and Tientsin Military Organs Will Be Relocated to Serve as a Sino-Japanese Buffer Zone is Not the Central Government's Intention. It Seems to Be a Groundless Rumor. (17th Dispatch)

(Tsinan) At 9:40, Huang Fu, Ho Chi-kung and His Party's Special Train Headed North. Han Fu-chü Arrived at the Station to See Them Off. (17th Dispatch)

(Tsinan) Huang Fu Told People in Tsinan Yesterday That He Has a Way to Break the Stalemate in North China. (17th Dispatch)

(Tsinan) Liu Shou-chung is Scheduled to Depart on the 18th to Visit Chou Village, Tzu Chuan, Poshan, Weihsien, Tsingtao, and Yantai. (17th Dispatch)

(Hsüchow) Huang Fu Passed Hsüchow on the Pingpu Train This Morning on the 17th and Headed North. Wang Ke-min Had Gone North Ahead of Huang. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) The Newly Appointed Chairman of the Peiping Political Reorganization Committee, Huang Fu, Arrived in Peiping at 4:35 PM Today. Ho Ying-chin and Other Government Personnel Went to Welcome Him. Huang Told Chinese Reporters That He Denied That He Had Come North This Time to Conduct Reconciliation Talks With Japan, and Said That He Would Abide by the Central Government's Policy to Deal With the Situation in North China. His First Task Was to Stabilize the Public Morale in North China. According to Local Evening Newspapers, This Morning, When Huang's Special Train Entered Tientsin Station, a Young Man Threw a Bomb on the Railway Overpass, Resulting in Injuries to Two Soldiers. The Railway Overpass Was Also Damaged, But the Special Train Was Unharmed. The Bomber Was Apprehended on the Spot, But Did Not Confess. Therefore, When Huang Arrived in Peiping, the Station Was Temporarily Under Martial Law to Prevent Accidents. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

Tientsin City Last Night

Two Sudden Loud Noises 19

Japanese Army Issues Plainclothes Team Firearms

(Tientsin) According to a Certain Source, The Plainclothes Team of the Japanese Concession Had Received Firearms and Issued Passwords on the Evening of the 17th. There Were Extraordinary Preparations in the Japanese Military Barracks. The Atmosphere Was Extremely Tense. Shops in the Vicinity of the Government Building and City Hall Were Closed at 9 PM, and Pedestrians Disappeared From the Roads. At 8:40 PM, a Sudden Loud Noise Reverberated, Shaking the Entire City. Enquiries Around Various Places Yielded No Reports. It Was Undoubtedly Issued From the Japanese Concession. (17th Dispatch)

Puppet Army of Liu Kuei-tang's Unit

Preparing to Attack Changpei 20

(Peiping) Changpei Dispatch, The Japanese Side Ordered Liu Kuei-tang's Unit to Attack Changpei From Dolon, Intending to Seize Kalgan. Liu Kuei-tang is Preparing to Mobilize, and Forced Chang Hai-peng's Unit to Attack Kuyüan, Chihkeng, and Lungkuan From P'ingning. Liu and Chang's Two Units Jointly Attacked Kalgan. Chang's Unit First Dispatched Two Branches, Namely the Chuan Yü-fen and Ying Fei Cavalry Units, a Total of 4,000 Troops, on the 12th From Fengning, Scheduled to Arrive at Tatan on the 17th. Tang Yü-lin Has Ordered the Cavalry of Chao Brigade and Shih Brigade, and the Infantry of Tung Brigade to Firmly Defend the Foremost Defensive Areas, Surveying Defensive Works, Extending Over Ten Miles. Tang Expressed His Determination to Firmly Defend Chahar East With Feng Chan-hai's Unit. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Feng Chan-hai Came to Peiping From the Kuyüan Paochang Defense Area and Visited Ho Ying-chin to Report on Defense Affairs. (17th Dispatch)

Japanese Intentions Towards North China

There is Talk of Joint International Administration of North China 21

(Peiping) Although it is Difficult to Predict Whether the Japanese Army's Intentions in Pressuring Near Peking With Heavy Troops Are to Occupy Peiping and Tientsin, It is Inevitable That They Want to Force Our Country to Submit and Obey. However, Our Side is Determined Not to Submit. Currently, There Are Three Theories From the Japanese Side About North China. (1) Pu Yi Entering the Pass to Ascend the Throne. (2) New Organization of Traitors Like Li Chi-chun and Chang Pi. (3) Following the Precedent of the Boxer Protocol and Asking Various Countries to Temporarily Jointly Administer North China, With the Japanese as the Center of Gravity, and Then Appoint Chinese People to Local Government Affairs. It is Difficult to Predict Which of the Three Theories Will Prevail. It is Heard That When Yoshizawa Came to Peiping Last Time, He Tried to Persuade Various Ambassadors With Joint Administration. It is Unknown What the Results Were. (17th Dispatch)

(Peiping) There is Talk That Shih Yu-san Has Already Defected to the Puppet State and is Coordinating in Chinhuangtao. Traitors are Everywhere. Since the Incident of Buying Assassins in Yu Hsueh-chung's Affair, Military and Political Officials Are Wary. (17th Dispatch)

Wu Tieh-cheng Talks About Current Affairs 22

(Nanking) Wu Tieh-cheng Said That Recently the Japanese Bandits Have Occupied Shihhsia, and Peiping and Tientsin Have Suddenly Become Critical. Some of My Countrymen Believe That Peiping and Tientsin Cannot Be Protected in the End, or That After the Enemy Occupies Peiping and Tientsin, the Central Government Will Change Its Attitude. In Fact, These Are All Mistakes. The Central Government's Long-Term Resistance Policy Will Never Change. Although the Enemy Has the Upper Hand Now, It Will Not Be Easy for Them to Acquire Peiping and Tientsin. Even if Peiping and Tientsin Are Lost by Any Chance, for the Sake of Our Country's Dignity, We Must Retaliate With a Do-or-Die Battle. Generalissimo Chiang Has Long Planned to Divide His Troops to Go North to Rescue North China and Recover Lost Territories. Therefore, He Has Entrusted the Task of Suppressing Bandits to the Three Route Commanders-in-Chief of the South, Northwest, and West, With the Southern Route Being Particularly Important to the Overall Situation of Suppressing Bandits. However, Recently, I Heard That the Southern Route's Commander-in-Chief and Deputy Commander-in-Chief, Chen Chi-tang and Bai Chongxi, Have Both Indicated That They Will Not Take Office. If This is True, It Will Inevitably Increase the Difficulty of Resisting Japan, Which is Truly Regrettable. In Short, With a Great Enemy Before Us, Who is an Enemy and Who is a Friend is Easiest to Understand. We Should Unite Immediately to Resist Foreign Aggression and Save the Country. Otherwise, When the Nest is Overturned, There Will Be No Intact Eggs. It Will Be Too Late to Regret. I Have No Intention of Going North. (17th Dispatch)

Various Circles in the Capital

Oppose Russia Selling the East Road 23

The Puppet Deputy Foreign Minister Ohashi Arrives in Tokyo to Consult With the Government

The Manchouli Middle East Road Club is Set on Fire

(Nanking) The Anti-Japanese Association of Various Circles in the Capital Believes That Soviet Russia Has Violated International Faith and Is Arbitrarily Seeking to Sell the Middle East Road, Which is In Effect Helping Japan to Seize Our Country's Rights and Interests, in Order to Win the Favor of Japanese Warlords and Avoid Their Threats. It Specially Issued a Nationwide Telegram on the 17th, Unanimously and Firmly Opposing It. (17th Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Puppet Manchukuo's Deputy Foreign Minister Ohashi Tadashi, Because of the East Road Issue and Other Important Issues That Need to Be Agreed Upon With the Japanese Side, Arrived at Tokyo Station at 4 PM Today. (17th Telecommunications Dispatch)

(Harbin) The Manchouli Middle East Railway Employees' Club Was Destroyed by Fire Yesterday, With Losses Reaching About 120,000 Rubles. It Is Heard That It Was Caused by Arson, But No One Was Arrested. (16th Reuters Dispatch)

Kung Hsiang-hsi

Assisting With the Ministry of Finance's Political Affairs 24

(Nanking) After Sung Tzu-wen Went to the United States, He Will Take a Ship to England to Attend the World Economic Conference. Regarding the Affairs of the Ministry of Finance, When Sung Was About to Leave, the National Government Ordered the Ministry's Deputy Minister of Political Affairs, Tsou Lin, to Temporarily Act as His Agent. The Ministry of Finance Received a Telegram From Sung From the United States Yesterday, Briefly Stating That the Date of His Return to China After Attending the British Economic Conference Still Needs to Be Awaited. Because the Ministry of Finance's Fundraising is Important, He Requested That the Newly Appointed President of the Central Bank, Kung Hsiang-hsi, Assist With Everything. Kung Has Agreed to Slightly Intervene in the Affairs of the Ministry of Finance Before Sung Returns to China. (17th Dispatch)

Chen Shao-kuan Talks About

Tientsin Naval Hospital Case 25

(Nanking) Naval Chief Chen Shao-kuan Spoke About: (1) Regarding the Case of Chang Hsueh-liang Stealing and Selling the Tientsin Naval Hospital, Although the Central Government Has Negotiated, Not Only Has the Tientsin French Consulate Ignored It, But It Has Also Demolished Most of the Buildings, Demarcated a Part of the Base, and Sold It at a High Price, Using the Proceeds From the Sale to Build Kuanma Road. This Kind of Sticking Plaster Action is Opposed by My Ministry to the End. As For the Recovery Method, It is Currently Divided Into Two Steps. One is Negotiation, and the Other is Force. The First Method is Currently Being Adopted, With the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Negotiating With Them. As For Whether to Adopt the Second Method, It Depends on the Results of the First Method of Negotiation. (2) The Defense of Shanghai, Wuhan, and Various Ports in the Yangtze River Basin is Solid, and the River Defense is Peaceful. (3) The Situation in Peiping and Tientsin is Critical. My Army is Fighting Bravely and Can Certainly Achieve the Effect of Turning Danger Into Safety. In Any Case, There is Absolutely No Room for Direct Negotiations Between China and Japan. External Criticism is Groundless and Speculative. (17th Dispatch)

Northern Ning Road Manager

Thomasen Passes Away 26

(Tientsin) Northern Ning Road Manager Thomasen Had Been Ill For Several Weeks and Was Hospitalized for Treatment. This Afternoon, He Seemed Very Happy, But in the Afternoon, a Gunshot Was Heard in His Room. Upon Entering to Look, Thomasen Had Passed Away. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

Kiangsi Provincial Government Will Be Reorganized 27

Liu Shih Succeeds Kiangsi Chairman

(Nanking) Kiangsi Province Will Be Reorganized. Hsiung Shih-hui Will Be Transferred to the Chief of Staff of the Headquarters. Liu Chih is Proposed to Succeed as Chairman of Kiangsi. The Four Department Heads Have Been Determined: Civil Affairs - Chang Ting-pan, Finance - Li Wen-hao, Education - Cheng Tien-fang, Construction - Kung Tzu-sui. (17th Dispatch)

Mexican Anti-Chinese

Central Government Considers Response 28

(Nanking) In Recent Years, Overseas Chinese in Mexico Have Been Subjected to Abuse by the Mexican Side, and Most Have Been Expelled Back to China. The Situation is Serious. A Reporter Visited a Certain Authority to Ask About the Truth. According to the Interview, in Recent Years, Both Shunshan Provinces in Mexico Have Expelled Overseas Chinese. The Embassy in Mexico Has Negotiated Seriously, But the Mexican Central Government Has No Power to Stop It. Negotiations With Various Provinces Have Been Ineffective. Two Years Ago, They Tried to Have the US Government Act as a Mediator, But It Could Not Be Carried Out Due to Mexican Opposition. Last Year, They Planned to Appeal to the League of Nations, But the Mexican Side Claimed That the Overseas Chinese Were Unwilling to Obey the Regulations and Voluntarily Closed Their Businesses and Went Elsewhere, and Did Not Admit That There Were Arrests and Abuses, So It Was Inconvenient to Bring It Up. Later, They Planned to Start From the Beginning of a Treaty, and Issued a Draft of the Sino-Mexican Treaty, Ordering the Embassy in Mexico to Discuss It With the Mexican Government, But There is Still No Progress. A Month Ago, the Anti-Chinese Headquarters in Mexico City Issued a Declaration, Advising the Anti-Chinese Parties in Good Provinces to Adopt More Moderate Measures, But With No Results. Recently, Some Suggested to the Central Government That the Path of Negotiation Has Been Exhausted, and Requested That Decisive Measures Be Taken. However, Regarding Mexico's Interests in China, Our Actions Seem to Need to Be Considered Carefully. In Short, the Central Government Has Always Been Concerned About the Overseas Chinese in Mexico. However, the Policies and Methods to Deal With It Must Be Carefully Considered to Achieve Practical Results. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Cheerfully Send Off the Anti-Japanese Army of Three Provinces to Go North 29

The 19th Route Army Set Off to Enter Hunan

(Hong Kong) Various Circles in Kwangtung Held a Cheerfully Send Off Meeting for the Anti-Japanese Army of Three Provinces Going North at the Central University Playground This Afternoon. Tens of Thousands of People Attended. After a Representative of the Executive Committee, Cheng Pi-chuan, Delivered a Farewell Speech, He Gave Three Banners of Loyalty and Bravery in Killing the Enemy to the Kwangtung, Kwangsi, and Fukien Armies. The Crowd Shouted, "Return My Mountains and Rivers," The Situation Was Extremely Solemn. (17th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The 19th Route Army Set Off From Lochang on the 18th to Enter Hunan. The Kwangtung Pan Piao Regiment Took a Car to Shaochou on the 17th. The Li Heng-chung and Chao Lan Regiments Will Go North on the 20th and 25th Respectively. Teng Lung-kuang is Scheduled to Depart on the 27th. The Vanguard Team of the Kwangsi Tan Lien-fang Division Arrived in Quanzhou on the 15th. The Deputy Commander of the Kwangtung, Kwangsi, and Fukien Anti-Japanese Army Innerly Ordered Teng. (17th)

Current Commentary

Peace in Tianjin, North China and the Overall Situation 30

— From Germany

In recent days, the enemy's situation has become increasingly urgent. Shixia has fallen, they have crossed the Luan River, Tangshan has been abandoned, and Miyun has been bombed. Tianjin and Beijing are already in a precarious position of being overlooked from a height. Furthermore, internal spies are lurking, willingly acting as accomplices to the enemy, and the people's hearts are restless, making it impossible to feel secure even for a single day. I have yet to see any comprehensive defense plan from the government, and the few troops on the front lines who are fighting hard for a long time have already reached the end of their strength. In fact, they are definitely powerless to defend this dangerous city under the enemy's gaze. The enemy has declared, "We must obtain Tianjin and Beijing." We look north with longing, truly overwhelmed with worry and fear, and even more so with grief and indignation.

If Tianjin and Beijing are lost, then North China will be difficult to protect. If North China is not protected, then the entire situation of our country will be shaken. This connection is as clear as pointing at one's palm, with no room for doubt. Therefore, the current crisis in Tianjin and Beijing is already a matter of life and death for our entire nation. The severity of the situation is no longer comparable to the fall of Liaoning and Jilin, and the loss of Rehe. If we still regard it with indifference and remain unconcerned, then in the blink of an eye, our country will inevitably follow in the footsteps of Annam and Korea. Once the country is destroyed, the nation will be reduced to slaves. At that time, even if we want to love and save our country, it will be impossible.

However, judging from the current situation, we cannot help but believe that our entire country, from top to bottom, seems to have already resigned itself to becoming slaves of a conquered nation. From beginning to end, the government has not shown any comprehensive defense plan, but only uses a small number of troops to resist the powerful enemy in what seems like a childish game. Day after day, new defensive positions are established; day after day, strategic retreats are made. As a result, the enemy approaches daily, we retreat daily, our territory shrinks daily, and the national crisis deepens daily. This dangerous state is truly unprecedented. Two months ago, the ancient artifacts of Beiping were already being shipped south in batches. Currently, various schools in Tianjin and Beijing are also planning to move south, while the land and the people are disregarded. What is the intention? What is the plan? We truly cannot fathom the depths of their minds. What is even more painful is that the country is in such danger, yet the Sichuan Rebellion has erupted again. The entire country exerts itself to kill each other, and remains indifferent to the great enemy at hand. Alas! Cooking beans to burn the beanstalk, slaughtering each other behind closed doors, those close to us are heartbroken, and our enemies rejoice. With the fishermen watching around us, will we ultimately become the snipe and the clam?

As for our people, they seem to be content with temporary peace and security, and do not care about national affairs at all. Recalling the January 28th Incident of last year, Shanghai was under the ravages of artillery fire, Zhabei was reduced to scorched earth, and the enemy and our forces fought to the death with blood and flesh. The people of Shanghai witnessed it with shock and awe. However, other parts of Shanghai remained indifferent, indulging in pleasure and poison, as if everything were normal. Today, Tianjin and Beijing are in a state of emergency, and people's hearts are in turmoil. However, outside of Tianjin and Beijing, people are still singing and dancing, as if nothing is happening. Even in Shanghai, the decadent music, the fox trot dances, the extravagance and intoxication, are causing people to forget death and indulge in pleasure. "The singing girls do not know the hatred of a fallen nation, and across the river they still sing 'The Flowers of the Rear Courtyard'." Faced with this kind of utterly inappropriate and strange phenomenon, we can only beat our chests and cry in anguish.

In this world, only death and national subjugation cannot be experienced. Because people cannot be brought back to life after death, and a country that has been destroyed is not easy to restore. Moreover, once a person dies, everything is over, and the dead are no longer in pain. As for national subjugation, the entire nation is reduced to beasts of burden and slaves, unable to seek death or survive. The pain and suffering are beyond imagination. The people of our country are indulging in pleasure and poison today, and remain indifferent to the country's peril, as if they have not yet tasted the bitterness of national subjugation. India, Egypt, Korea, and Burma are all vivid examples before our eyes. What kind of suffering and pain did they encounter?

In short, the current crisis in Tianjin and Beijing is not a local problem of Tianjin and Beijing, but a whole problem related to the life and death of our entire country. Saving Tianjin and Beijing is to save North China, and saving North China is to save China. The times are critical and the situation is pressing. We must urgently make a comprehensive plan and a comprehensive strategy. This is the last and only opportunity. Our government and our people must have a final awakening and make a final plan.

Central Political Council 31

Five New Members Added to the Beiping Military Branch

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 357th meeting at 9:00 AM on the 17th. Attendees included Ju Zheng, Chen Guofu, Wang Zhaoming, Sun Ke, Ye Chucang, Wu Tiecheng, Wang Zhengting, Chen Zhaoying, Chen Shuren, Chen Gongbo, Zhou Qigang, Enhe Batu, Zhu Jiahua, Chu Minyi, and more than thirty others. It was resolved to pass it and hand it over to the Military Affairs Committee. (2) The Political, Military, and Legal Systems Groups reported and reviewed a case regarding which agency should review military officers if they are impeached. It was decided that it should be reviewed by the Central Supreme Military Agency. The decision was passed. (3) Ji Yiqiao, Hu Yukun, Zou Zuohua, Zhang Huanxiang, Gao Weiyue, and Liu Shangqing were appointed as members of the Beiping Branch of the Military Affairs Committee. It was also resolved that the Yellow River Conservancy Commission's monthly operating expenses of 50,000 yuan should be allocated by the provinces of Hebei, Hubei, and Henan, and that the establishment fee of 100,000 yuan should be allocated by the Ministry of Finance. (Special dispatch, 17th)

In the near future, he will convene relevant agencies to discuss the organizational direction, the candidates for chairman and provincial committee members, and funding issues. President Roosevelt Sends to Fifty-Four Nations

Declaration Guaranteeing World Peace 33

Advising Acceptance of MacDonald Disarmament Plan

Countries Guarantee Their Troops Will Not Cross Borders

The U.S. Wholeheartedly Endorses the Conclusion of a Consultation Convention

Historical Changes in American Foreign Policy 34

(Washington) U.S. President Roosevelt's declaration calling for world peace guarantees, the outline of which was reported yesterday, was sent directly to the heads of state of 54 nations, going beyond the Geneva forum. It serves as a warning to Europe about the dangers of continuing to bargain for national interests within the disarmament conference, and aims to eliminate the signs of failure of the future World Economic Conference. In addition to advising the world to accept British Prime Minister MacDonald's disarmament proposal as the first step to avoid war, it also invites countries to independently guarantee that they will not send armed forces outside their borders, and attaches a powerful warning: If any powerful country refuses to clearly record its willingness to oppose aggressive behavior, then when disaster strikes in the future, the world will know where the blame lies, and hopes that countries will not bear this heavy responsibility.

Consultation Convention 35

The British disarmament plan stipulates a consultation system. This move by the US President shows that the American foreign policy of strictly refusing to be bound by consultation conventions has undergone significant changes.

Peace Guarantee 36

In addition, the US President also proposed that at a time when the disarmament machinery of the whole world is operating tirelessly under the British plan, existing armaments and forces should not be increased any further. Countries should solemnly guarantee that their combat weapons will not be increased. President Roosevelt stated in the document that during the entire period of arms reduction, world peace must be guaranteed. Therefore, I propose a fourth step, which will run concurrently with these three proposals, and will rely entirely on the faithful implementation of these three proposals and be bound by existing treaty rights.

Three Suggestions 37

I propose that all countries of the world conclude a solemn and effective non-aggression pact. I also propose that all countries solemnly reaffirm their obligations to limit and reduce armaments. I further propose that if all signatory countries can faithfully fulfill this obligation, then each country should agree not to send armed forces of any kind beyond its borders.

Clearly Define Responsibility 38

The US President also warned countries, saying that common sense tells us that if any powerful country refuses to join the worldwide joint effort with true sincerity to ensure political and economic peace, then these two major joint efforts, one in Geneva and one in London, will be hindered and will not make progress. Once this happens, the civilized world, which is thirsty for both kinds of peace, will know who is responsible for the failure. I urge all countries not to bear this heavy responsibility, and hope that the countries participating in the two major conferences will translate their declared policies into action.

Finally, the US President pointed out that at a time when everyone urgently needs to shoulder the heavy responsibility of maintaining world peace, small obstacles should be removed, small objectives should be abandoned, and concluded by stating that I believe your government will be able to join in realizing this hope.

Communication with Soviet Russia 39

This document from the US President was sent directly to the heads of state of 54 nations, including Soviet Russia, and was addressed directly to Mikhail Kalinin, Chairman of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union. It is worth noting that this is the first time that an American president has directly addressed a document to an unrecognized country. Some commentators believe that it fully demonstrates President Roosevelt's urgent desire to convene the world to jointly plan for the great cause of peace.

This document is currently being recorded and sent to Congress for reference, because if the United States joins any international agreement, it must be approved by the Senate. Before issuing this document yesterday, Roosevelt met with several Senate leaders for a long time, and it is expected that he has already obtained the Senate's assurance that it will approve the United States' joining the proposed pact.

Eliminate Disorder 40

Furthermore, the US President's appeal for peace guarantees is actually intended to achieve the complete victory of the World Economic Conference. Therefore, in the document, when discussing international relations, he stated that countries have convened two major conferences to eliminate the disorder in the economic world. The World Economic Conference will be held soon and must quickly end. The world cannot sit and wait for protracted discussions. The conference must stabilize currency values, allow free flow of world trade, and jointly raise commodity prices internationally in order to establish order and eliminate existing disturbances. We must slightly restrain our individual domestic plans and work together for wise and thoughtful international action to promote economic recovery. The disarmament conference has been going on for more than a year and has not yet achieved satisfactory results. Various confusing proposals are still in dangerous conflict.

Restore Prosperity 41

Our responsibility today lies in seeking practical and feasible results through joint action, based on the greatest welfare of the greatest number. It must be known that the lives, happiness, and prosperity of men, women, and children all over the world depend on the decisions of the governments in the near future. He then pointed out the impact of disarmament on the economic conference. How can we calmly decide economic issues if there are other entanglements before us? He also said that countries establish armaments for only two reasons: a small number of countries want to acquire the territory of neighboring countries, but the majority are afraid of aggression by others. Modern offensive weapons are far sharper than defensive weapons, and this fear is justified. Therefore, if all countries can fully agree not to use offensive weapons, then national defense will naturally be as solid as a golden soup, and the borders and independence of each country will be secure, and the fear of aggression by others will naturally disappear. (National Telegraph, 16th)

Non-Aggression Pact Aimed at the World 42

(Washington) While supporting the British disarmament proposal, President Roosevelt still advocates that in the event of aggressive behavior, the United States should consult with other countries based on the Kellogg-Briand Pact. It is said that the proposed non-aggression pact is aimed at the entire world, not at any one country. (Reuters telegram, 16th)

A Great Monument in the History of the Peace Movement

Governments of All Countries Praise Roosevelt's Extraordinary Action 43

MacDonald Believes It is a Remarkable Appeal

Soviet Russia is Completely Surprised and Especially Pleased

Stubborn Germany Also Expresses Approval

The Italian Government Announces Unconditional Acceptance

Only France Remains Skeptical and Silent

(Washington) Governments of various countries have responded with acceptance of the proposals and praise for the policies in President Roosevelt's appeal for a guarantee of peace. Even Germany, which has been most stubborn on disarmament and prompted the U.S. President to take this extraordinary action, has expressed its approval. German officials generally believe that this document has opened a path to resolving disputes.

In London, British Prime Minister MacDonald, speaking at a meeting of the St. George's Society, told the American women present that he welcomed the U.S. President's declaration, considering it a remarkable appeal, and said that this move by the U.S. President would be a great monument in the history of the peace movement. With this declaration from the U.S., it will no longer disregard matters related to world peace. At the same time, the British Prime Minister also declared that although Britain supports Germany's lifting of current restrictions, its future attitude will depend largely on Germany's actions and less on Germany's self-proclaimed desire for peace.

News from Moscow: Russia received this document completely unexpectedly. Since the revolution, this is the first time that there has been a direct communication between the United States and Russia. Political leaders all said that the U.S. President's appeal was direct and to the point, and welcomed it as a means of achieving international understanding, and regarded this move as an indication of removing obstacles that have prevented the exchange of views between the U.S. and Russia. Officials generally felt gratified and expected that the resumption of diplomatic relations between the U.S. and Russia would be a matter of time.

News from Rome: Italian authorities claimed that Italy unconditionally accepted this proposal, as Italian Prime Minister Mussolini believed that the situation created by the disarmament conference was one of the most dangerous that the world had seen in many years, and believed that if there was no significant progress towards peace at this time, countries would be plunged into extreme turmoil.

Disarmament delegates in Geneva praised the President's courage and魄力. Before German Chancellor Hitler explained Germany's attitude towards rearmament to the Reichstag, he directly appealed to the whole world for a guarantee of peace. It is expected that the U.S. President's proposal will be able to moderate the German Chancellor's speech.

A spokesperson for the Mexican government announced tonight that the Mexican government will instruct its representative in Geneva to follow the peace principles put forward by the U.S. President and support his proposal at the disarmament conference. It also said that the country's economic situation currently appears to have made great progress. If so, it will allow Mexico to remain within the League of Nations. Mexico had intended to withdraw from the League of Nations because the burden of membership fees was too heavy.

France seems to be skeptical of the U.S. President's proposal. Although government officials have remained silent, many politicians in the opposition say that they fear that unconditional acceptance will weaken France's position, and believe that France can only accept this kind of proposal after Germany modifies its armaments requirements. If Germany does not change its armaments requirements, then the responsibility for the failure of the disarmament conference should be borne by Germany. (National Telegraph, 16th)

Rome: President Roosevelt's declaration has had a great effect in Italy. It is generally felt that it is difficult for any country to reject this proposal and bear the responsibility for destroying disarmament. (Reuters telegram, 16th)

(Geneva) Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson welcomed the U.S. President's request, saying that if governments of all countries agree, a disarmament convention should be concluded quickly. (Reuters telegram, 16th)

(Paris) Today, the exchange market price rose slightly, all thanks to the U.S. President's declaration. It is generally felt that this declaration is very timely and can make German Chancellor Hitler deliberate on his speech to be delivered to the Reichstag on Wednesday. (Reuters telegram, 16th)

(Geneva) Today, a representative of the Little Entente said that although most of the major powers have responded to the U.S. President's declaration, the two issues of France's security and Germany's equality of armaments still exist. Therefore, it is not surprising here that France is not immediately enthusiastic about the U.S. President's proposal not to send troops out of the country. If President Roosevelt's intention is for the United States to join a truly effective consultation convention, then the disarmament conference may be saved. However, it is expected that France and the Little Entente will still insist on concluding a security convention and continue to oppose Germany's demand for the right to rearm. Also, observers here expect that the United States may not be unable to agree to participate in military action under a consultation convention. Therefore, there is hope here that the position taken by the United States will have the effect of moderating Germany's change of strategy, so that a disarmament agreement that satisfies the French can be signed. If Hitler can moderate his demands and abandon his war-like language, he may be able to remove obstacles and open a path to understanding based on the U.S. President's proposals. (National Telegraph, 16th)

Roosevelt's Message to Congress 44

(Washington) After issuing his declaration and request to the 44 nations, President Roosevelt issued an equally important document to Congress, saying that he put forward the proposal for a world non-aggression pact because he gradually saw that the guarantee of world political and economic peace and stability was now threatened by selfish and short-sighted policies and actions. The American people's deep-rooted expectations for a better life situation and their desire to avoid war are shared by the people of all countries. To achieve this goal, it is necessary to reduce armaments and completely abolish the tools that can make war successful. Only then can the invasion of any other country and the destruction of national sovereignty be prevented. All countries now understand this meaning, because there must be this abolition, and only then can small countries be comparatively less harmed by big countries. The lack of government funds and the crisis of bankruptcy are caused primarily by the excessive number of troops, and the only thing that can prevent aggression is disarmament. The American people understand that if other countries have aggressive weapons, then they need aggressive weapons themselves; if other countries are willing to give up aggressive weapons, they are willing to give them up themselves. (Reuters telegram, 16th)

Original Text of the Peace Application 45

Transmitted to Our Government Yesterday by the U.S. Embassy

Visionary and Pioneering Historical Initiative

Important Change in American Foreign Policy

(Nanjing) U.S. President Roosevelt sent a joint application to the heads of state of 44 countries around the world (including the Soviet Union) on the 16th, asking all countries to reduce armaments, absolutely abolish aggressive weapons, and agree to stop armed troops from crossing borders, in order to save the failure of the disarmament conference and promote the success of the World Economic Conference. This is truly a visionary and great move, and it is also a very important indication of recent American foreign policy. The request to National Government Chairman Lin was sent to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for submission by U.S. Embassy Counselor Peck at 5 PM on the 17th. The original text is translated as follows:

To Chairman Lin of the National Government of the Republic of China,

As the head of the American government, I, based on the deep hopes of my own people, address you and ask you to convey to the Chinese people what this hope is: to maintain peace through feasible disarmament methods, and to make our joint efforts to overcome the economic chaos victorious. To achieve this goal, all countries have convened two major world conferences. The happiness, prosperity, and even the lives of men, women, and children in this world depend on the decisions that each country's government will take in the near future. The improvement of social conditions, the protection of human rights, and the development of social justice all depend on this decision. The World Economic Conference is about to open and will make a decision immediately, because the world cannot allow this decision-making process to be delayed any longer. The conference must find ways to change the current chaotic situation and stabilize it. The methods are nothing more than stabilizing the monetary system, allowing free movement of world commerce, and using international cooperation to raise commodity prices. In short, the conference should use wise and prudent international actions to assist each country's individual domestic plans to restore the economy. The disarmament conference has been meeting for more than a year, but has not been able to achieve satisfactory results. Differences of opinion with each other still present dangerous conflicts. Therefore, our responsibility is to act together to achieve practical results based on the greatest happiness for the majority of the people. In the face of this extraordinary responsibility, all small obstacles and objectives should be eliminated. Whoever triumphs because of selfishness will ultimately fail. Wherever there is progress towards lasting peace in the world for those of us who live together, it is the only thing worth our efforts. Despite the lessons of the European War and its cruel circumstances, the burden of armaments on the people of all countries in the world today is heavier than at any time before. Let us ask the reason for these armaments. Clearly, there are only two reasons: One is that some governments have clear or hidden objectives to expand their territory at the expense of their neighbors. I dare to believe that governments with such objectives are only a few. The second is fear of aggression by other countries. I dare to believe that most countries feel the need to maintain excessive armaments not because they intend to invade other countries, but because they fear aggression by other countries. This fear is justified, because modern offensive weapons are far stronger than modern defensive weapons. Structures like fortresses, electrical nets, and coastal defenses are suitable for defense, but they are easily destroyed if attacked by aircraft, heavy artillery, tanks, and poison gas cannons. If all countries in the world can agree to stop equipping and using effective offensive weapons, then defensive work will naturally become inviolable, and the borders and independence of each country will naturally be safe. The complete abolition of offensive weapons is the ultimate goal of the disarmament conference. The effective reduction of several or many kinds of offensive weapons is the immediate goal of the disarmament conference. This government dares to believe that the strategies for immediately reducing aggressive weapons that are currently being discussed in Geneva are only the first step in reaching the ultimate goal. We do not believe that the steps proposed to be implemented immediately are sufficient, but this government still welcomes the methods currently proposed and is willing to continue to take further steps in disarmament to achieve success. In short, the following three steps should be agreed upon in the current discussions: (1) To achieve this goal, the first definite measure should be taken immediately, as broadly specified in the MacDonald Plan. (2) Time and procedure should be agreed upon to complete the overall method. (3) During the first step and subsequent methods, no country shall increase its armaments above the limits prescribed by the treaty. However, world peace must be guaranteed during the entire period of disarmament. Therefore, I propose a fourth step. This step is in line with the faithful performance of the above proposals and in accordance with existing treaties, that is, all countries of the world should participate in a solemn and certain non-aggression pact, and solemnly reaffirm their obligations to restrict and reduce armaments, and when the signatory countries can faithfully fulfill their obligations, each agrees not to send armed forces of any kind beyond its borders. Speaking in common sense, if any powerful country does not participate in the joint efforts for political and economic peace in Geneva and London with genuine sincerity, then progress will be blocked and will ultimately be unsuccessful. Under these circumstances, the civilized countries of the world that are currently seeking the above two ways of peace will know where the responsibility for failure lies. I wish that no country will assume this responsibility, and that the participants in these two major conferences will put their declared policies into practice. This is the path to political and economic peace, and I am certain that your government will participate in the achievement of these desires.

Roosevelt, (Special dispatch, 17th)

Militarists Alone Have Many Dissenting Opinions

Roosevelt's Telegram Reaches the Emperor of Japan; Japanese Government Takes a Cautious Attitude 46

International Conference Planned; Convention on Consultation Can Be Considered

Military Actions Across Borders Difficult to Acknowledge

Holding onto Manchuria, Reserving Rights to Expand Armaments

(Tokyo) Today, the spokesperson for the Japanese Army Ministry criticized President Roosevelt's declaration, stating that a guarantee of peace, which maintains the status quo without addressing environmental solutions, is unacceptable to Japan. Japan can agree to the proposal of not increasing armaments during meetings, but considers it unfortunate that countries cannot send troops beyond their borders, as this would hinder Japan's current actions in North China. The Foreign Ministry, besides recognizing the importance of the US President's remarks, declined to comment further, as the President's message was addressed directly to the Japanese Emperor. (17th Reuters dispatch)

(Tokyo) US President Roosevelt's personal telegram guaranteeing peace arrived directly at the Imperial Palace this morning. Prime Minister Saitō and Foreign Minister Uchida immediately requested its release and, after discussing it with relevant ministries, will reply in the name of the Japanese government. The Japanese government will adopt a cautious attitude, avoiding explicit statements on their response policy before the message is released from the Imperial Palace. Therefore, the Japanese Foreign Ministry authorities have issued the following views on President Roosevelt's proposal in principle:

The British disarmament proposal is based on European standards and is not applicable to the Far East. However, before deliberating on the British proposal, Japan will maintain its insistence on first considering the Japanese proposal.

There is room for consideration of holding an international conference to establish a treaty of agreement in parallel with the Geneva Disarmament Conference.

Maintaining the status quo of armaments is not opposed in principle. However, according to the protocol, maintaining the security of Manchuria is necessary, so the minimum preparations and rights to expand related to this are reserved.

There is no objection to the impossibility of military actions across borders. However, the actions of Japanese troops on the Great Wall border originated from Chinese challenges and have no aggressive nature. If such defensive actions were also uniformly prohibited, it would not be suitable for the special circumstances of the Far East. (17th Den-tsu dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Army authorities generally hold the following views on President Roosevelt's personal telegram guaranteeing peace. In principle, there is no objection to the US President's opinion. However, the Soviet Union's propaganda of communism and China's boycott of goods are the root causes of war, and it is difficult for Japan, which is adjacent to such countries, to accept the notion that Japanese troops should not cross borders, ultimately recognizing the special circumstances. Furthermore, there is still an important question: the meaning and relationship of invoking the so-called right of self-defense, which hinders the Non-Aggression Treaty, must be clarified. (17th Den-tsu dispatch)

(Tokyo) The statement issued by US President Roosevelt to the heads of various countries was conveyed to the Foreign Ministry on the morning of the 17th by Debuchi, the Japanese ambassador to the UK. As there is no precedent for a US president to directly address the Japanese Emperor on diplomatic policy, the government has had various discussions and is currently considering the procedures to be adopted. (17th Nichiren dispatch)
