Eurasia Aviation Corporation Held a Memorial Service for Schmidt Yesterday 142

Walter Reports on Schmidt's Brief History

Li Jingcong Describes the Process of Jointly Establishing the Aviation Company

Schmidt, the Deputy Director and Chief of the Aviation Department of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation, died on April 29 in Germany during a long-distance test flight when the plane crashed and burned while flying over the Alps. Yesterday at 6:00 PM, the company held a special memorial service at the German Church at 1 Daxilu. Li Jingcong, the General Manager of the company, was sent by the Ministry of Transportation to attend as a representative. The details are as follows:

Venue Arrangement 143

A portrait of Mr. Schmidt was placed in the church, surrounded by many wreaths sent by various parties, including Tang Baoshu, Wen Hongen, Liu Hongsheng, Huang Naishu, Dai Enji, Huang Jiangquan, Xu Xueyu, Lin Wojiang, as well as the China Merchants Bureau, China National Aviation Corporation, the Directorate General of Posts, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation, the Telegraph Bureau, and the Chinese Aviation Association.

Attendees 144

Those who attended the memorial service yesterday included Dai Enji, the General Manager of the China National Aviation Corporation, Huang Baoqing, the Chief of the Operations Division, Tang Baoshu of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, Guo Zengliang, Cha Zhenhu, Liao Guanxuan, and Sun Mutang of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation, as well as the German directors of the company, Poolsen, Walter, Fanliek, and Fakell, Fukuoka, the representative of the German Chamber of Commerce, more than a hundred German residents in Shanghai, and the German Consul General in Shanghai also personally attended.

Report on Brief History 145

After playing mourning music, the service began with a prayer by the pastor of the church, followed by Walter, the Acting Chief of the Aviation Department of the company, who reported on Mr. Schmidt's brief history, which was translated into Mandarin by Liao Guanxuan. He said, "Today, we are holding a memorial service for Schmidt, and we have many thoughts. We admire Schmidt's boldness and spirit in running the aviation business. When the European War broke out, Schmidt returned to Germany to fight the enemy and fulfill his aviation responsibilities. He lost a leg while participating in the war. After fitting an artificial leg, he believed that Germany wanted to gain a position in the world and must promote aviation. His views were: (1) to use aviation to make transportation convenient and bring nations closer together, and (2) to spread Germany's scientific reputation to various countries. Schmidt had made flights over the Caucasus Mountains. Several years ago, in order to establish one of the world's largest aviation routes, the Eurasia Aviation Corporation, he came to China as the Eastern representative of the German Hansa Airlines to negotiate a postal transport contract. This contract is a model contract for Sino-foreign joint ventures. Schmidt was not just a theorist but also a practitioner, unafraid of danger and hardship, and moving forward courageously. He died in a plane crash in Germany during a long-distance test flight, sacrificing himself for aviation. Now, we should not be sad. We must continue Schmidt's spirit and move forward with effort."

Mr. Li's Speech 146

Following this, Li Jingcong, the General Manager of Eurasia Aviation Corporation and representative of the Ministry of Transportation, delivered a speech, saying: "Today, in my capacity as a representative of the Ministry of Transportation and the General Manager of Eurasia Aviation Corporation, I am here to attend the memorial service for Mr. Schmidt. Not only do we mourn Mr. Schmidt's sacrifice for the Sino-German joint venture, Eurasia Aviation, but we also mourn the loss of a good advisor in this aviation construction process for China, a country that has always been known for its close ties with Germany. We are well aware that Eurasia Aviation Corporation was established based on the long-term, open, and transparent negotiations between the Chinese Ministry of Transportation and Hansa Airways, which was closely related to the German Ministry of Transportation and entrusted by Mr. Schmidt, resulting in the signing of the Eurasia Aviation Mail Transport Agreement. However, we know little, or not in detail, about Mr. Schmidt's special vision and great aspirations during the negotiation of this agreement. In addition to my grief and mourning, I would like to briefly recount it for you. When the Ministry of Transportation was negotiating the agreement with Mr. Schmidt, the Sino-American Aviation Mail Transport Agreement, negotiated between China and the American Aviation Development Company, had already been signed. Although the Sino-American agreement at that time was also a joint venture, society at the time believed that it was entirely monopolized by the Americans. Mr. Schmidt deeply understood that utilizing foreign capital and talent to jointly develop Chinese enterprises was indeed the policy of the late Premier, but in operating a joint venture with China, which was vastly different from what it was before the 20th century, in order to ensure its smooth progress and prevent damage, it was essential to adhere to the principle of complete responsibility and command by the Chinese, with foreigners providing assistance. Otherwise, with the passage of time, it would inevitably arouse suspicion among the Chinese that foreigners were overstepping their bounds, and it would be difficult to achieve lasting harmony and cooperation. Therefore, he not only did not envy the special rights obtained by the American side under the contract, nor did he demand equal sharing of benefits, but he also actively expressed his support for the principle advocated by the Chinese Ministry of Transportation that the Chinese should hold two-thirds of the profit rights and the Germans should hold one-third of the profit rights. In other words, the Chinese should bear direct command and supervision responsibilities, and the Germans should bear the obligation of providing assistance in the Sino-German joint venture Eurasia Aviation. He believed that this principle was in line with the times and reversed the long-standing view of Europeans and Americans that Sino-foreign joint ventures could not succeed unless foreigners were directly responsible for handling them. In the end, this view proved to be a fallacy. Observing that the Eurasia agreement was still in the process of being negotiated, while the Sino-American agreement signed at that time had already been overturned by the Chinese opposition and had to be revised based on the principles stipulated in the Eurasia agreement, and that Eurasia Aviation Corporation has been established for three years according to the provisions of that agreement, not only has there been no difficulty in its operation, but its business has also seen daily development. This shows that Mr. Schmidt's disregard for conventions and his rejection of public opinion truly demonstrated his special vision. Furthermore, when negotiating the Eurasia agreement, Mr. Schmidt firmly believed that only a contract that did not contain the nature of control or monopoly could serve as a tool for genuine cooperation. He also hoped that the establishment of this agreement could encourage closer cooperation between China and Germany, that German companies intending to operate joint ventures in China could use this agreement as a blueprint for further development, that Sino-German industry and commerce could become more prosperous after the opening of Eurasia Aviation, and that cultural exchanges between Europe and Asia could become closer due to the convenience of transportation. Mr. Schmidt also deeply believed that China was vast and its transportation was obstructed, and that the construction of railways and the dredging of rivers would be costly and time-consuming, making it difficult to address the urgent needs. He hoped that after the signing of the Eurasia agreement, in addition to actively promoting the route from Shanghai, via Nanjing, Beijing, and Manchuria, to Europe via Russia, he also hoped that, to the extent possible, the route from Shanghai, via the inland and remote provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, and Xinjiang, and then via Russia to Europe, could also be promoted. Therefore, when the preparations for the Shanghai-Manchuria route were completed, he immediately proposed the establishment of a Northwest route to supplement the efforts of the Chinese government, pioneer the development of the interior's hidden resources, and relieve the suffering of the people in the interior. Mr. Schmidt's great aspirations can be seen from this. In order to realize his aspirations, Mr. Schmidt not only fulfilled his duties and made many proposals for the planning and preparation of Eurasia Aviation Corporation, but also personally conducted on-site surveys for each exploration flight, such as crossing the Hinggan Mountains and flying to Manchuria in the spring of the 20th year, flying across the Ruo Shui River and flying to Xinjiang in the winter of the same year, and the gradual trial flights to Shaanxi, Gansu, and Xinjiang from spring to winter last year. He never hesitated to endure hardship and personally face great dangers to obtain data for planning and preparation, making great contributions to China's aviation industry. The opening of China's Northwest route and its achievements today are all thanks to Mr. Schmidt. Even Mr. Schmidt's return to Germany this time was to prepare for the actual survey flight from Germany, leading a plane through Russia, and flying back to China to prepare for the official opening of Eurasia and realize his aspirations. Unfortunately, on April 29, he encountered danger and died in the line of duty while conducting a long-distance test flight in Germany, causing Eurasia Aviation Corporation to lose a pillar and China's aviation industry to lose a good assistant. In addition to our deep sorrow and mourning, we cannot help but admire Mr. Schmidt's special vision and great aspirations, and we hope that those of us who survive can continue to work hard based on his vision and aspirations to seek progress in all aspects between the two countries, so as to comfort Mr. Schmidt's spirit in heaven." Finally, a funeral march was played, and the meeting adjourned.

Interview with Various Parties Regarding the Concession Factory Inspection Case 147

Yu Hongjun said he will meet again soon

Bell said he is willing to negotiate at any time for a compromise

The consular body authorities deny that there is a compromise plan

Regarding the issue of factory inspections in the concessions, and the related matter of revising the bylaws of the Yangjingbang Regulations, its resolution is of great concern to Chinese and foreigners alike. After the consular body meeting the day before yesterday, it was rumored that a proper compromise had been reached. To clarify the truth for the public, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency specially visited the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Yu Hongjun, the Public Works Department and General Manager Bell, and the consular body authorities yesterday to inquire about the details. The details are recorded below.

Municipal Government Side 148

The True Situation Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Yu Hongjun, reiterated the Municipal Government's attitude and the progress made in the current resolution during an interview with a reporter from the New Voice News Agency yesterday. Yu said that the Municipal Government's attitude on this matter has been stated repeatedly and is quite clear, that the Municipal Government believes that factory inspection is of utmost importance and an urgent matter. Therefore, it is willing to negotiate a proper solution with the Public Works Department without violating China's sovereignty. The matter is currently under discussion. Mr. Feetham sent a written opinion to the Municipal Government some time ago, but this written opinion has not yet been received. He will meet with Feetham for further discussion after receiving it soon. This is the most recent true situation. As for the fact that the consular body has postponed the approval of the Yangjingbang Regulations at the request of the Chinese government, he does not know whether our side has indeed made this request because he has not received a report from the central government.

Public Works Department Side 149

Expresses Dissatisfaction A reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited Mr. Bell, General Manager of the Public Works Department, at his office yesterday and first asked him about the compromise plan for resolving the factory inspection issue reported in the newspaper. Mr. Bell replied that he was unaware of this matter and did not believe it, as the matter is currently awaiting a decision from the consular body. He then expressed dissatisfaction with the various inaccurate reports published in the newspapers in recent days, saying that he did not know what the purpose of the various exaggerated reports published in the newspapers recently was. He asked if Western newspapers were like this, and said that he did not take them seriously because what they published was incomprehensible.

Has Not Received a Reply However, Mr. Bell tacitly acknowledged that the consular body and the consular body will have a recommendation for resolving the factory inspection case. It is said that the draft amendments to the Yangjingbang Regulations have been sent to the consular body and the consular body for approval, but no reply has been received yet. The matter is currently awaiting a decision from the consular body.

Pre-Negotiation for a Compromise The reporter then inquired about the negotiations. Mr. Bell stated that the Public Works Department is quite willing to conduct negotiations with both parties to seek an appropriate solution. The start of negotiations does not necessarily have to wait until the consular body's recommendation is received; both parties can discuss at any time. As for whether the meeting between Yu Hongjun and Feetham last Friday was a formal negotiation or a private contact, Mr. Bell replied that it could be said to be a contact that was half official and half private.

Implement Inspection The reporter finally inquired about the date when the Public Works Department will implement factory inspection and whether it will be within this year. Mr. Bell replied that there is no doubt that this case will be implemented within this year, and the starting date is also quite near. Mr. Bell's statement seemed to be a casual reply in haste, as in fact, it is extremely difficult to implement without the consular body and the consular body approving the bylaws of the Yangjingbang Regulations, reaching an agreement on a solution with our side, and the Public Works Department itself having sufficient preparation for this matter. The so-called "starting date is quite near" is, in fact, impossible to achieve.

Consular Body Side 150

Denies Compromise Before visiting the General Manager of the Public Works Department yesterday, the reporter first visited the consular body authorities. Because the spokesperson refused to reveal their name, they only allowed the publication of official news. The spokesperson said that the consular body's meeting the day before yesterday only had a slight discussion on this issue and did not make any decisions regarding this matter. As for the reports that the meeting the day before yesterday decided that the Public Works Department would set up an inspection office and employ experienced Chinese people as inspectors, they are absolutely untrue. The meeting that day was a regular meeting, mainly to discuss other issues. In addition, the spokesperson said that the consular body has a recommendation on this matter, and the bylaws of the Yangjingbang Regulations, which have been approved by the consular body, have been sent to the consular body for consideration. No reply has been received yet, and there is no other compromise plan. As for the content of the recommendation, they refused to disclose it.

The Ministry of Industry's Statement 151

The New Voice News Agency's reporter stationed in Beijing visited the relevant authorities of the Ministry of Industry yesterday to inquire about the progress of the negotiations on the issue of factory inspection in the public concession. The authorities gave a detailed reply as follows:

Three Principles Decided Long Ago Since the national government announced the Factory Inspection Law in the 20th year, the Ministry of Industry has been preparing to gradually implement the measures. Regarding factory inspection in Shanghai, the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, the concession authorities, and international labor commissioners held three meetings at the end of the 20th year and decided on three principles: (1) The public concession and French concession authorities are willing to accept factory inspectors trained and recommended by the Chinese government to inspect factories in the concession. The aforementioned factory inspectors are supervised by central inspection personnel at any time. (2) Inspectors in the concession should report inspection results and difficulties to the Chinese government and the concession authorities on time. (3) All factory inspectors in the public concession and French concession of the municipal government should meet once a month to exchange opinions and jointly plan improvements. After these principles were decided, they were suddenly suspended because the Japanese consul submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Government to ban anti-Japanese movements. The sudden amendment of Article 34 of the bylaws of the Yangjingbang Land Regulations by the Western taxpayers' association, attempting to seize the right to inspect factories in the concession, not only infringed on China's sovereignty, but also contradicted the results of previous consultations. It seems that the concession authorities' move was rather abrupt.

The Public Works Department Has Understood After the Shanghai Municipal Government protested to the consuls, the concession authorities have shown considerable tolerance for the declaration of China's sovereignty. The Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Yu Hongjun, is responsible for negotiating with Feetham, the General Manager of the Public Works Department, and has presented the memorandum from the previous meeting for negotiation. Bao Guohua, a section chief of the Labor Division dispatched by the Ministry of Industry to Shanghai, only provided detailed opinions for the Municipal Government's preliminary negotiations. According to Bao's conversation with the New Voice News Agency's reporter stationed in Beijing after returning to Beijing, the Municipal Government and the Public Works Department are currently negotiating the principles for implementing factory inspection. This is currently in progress, so the content of the negotiations cannot be released. However, it can be said that the concession authorities are no longer as insistent on Article 34 of the bylaws of the Yangjingbang Regulations as before and are preparing to implement it. The concession authorities are also very clear about the sovereignty that the Chinese government is fighting for, so the future is quite promising.

Foreign Factories Still Need to Be Negotiated As for factory inspection in Shanghai, the preliminary inspection and investigation work in the Chinese-controlled areas has been completed. The Public Works Department has no objections to the inspection of Chinese-owned factories in the concession. However, the inspection of foreign factories in the concession is still a target for negotiation. The Ministry of Industry will never discriminate against domestic and foreign factories. Due to the importance of factory inspection, it is especially necessary to implement inspection. In the future, after the Shanghai Municipal Government and the concession authorities have negotiated to a considerable extent, the Ministry of Industry will also send representatives to attend the official consultation on the implementation of inspection measures.

Establish a Central Inspection Office The Ministry of Industry is also preparing to establish a Central Factory Inspection Office. However, the progress of the Shanghai Municipal Government's factory inspection does not have to wait until the Central Factory Inspection Office is established, because the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has already established an inspection section and all equipment can be implemented at any time.

Beijing and Shanghai Authorities Discuss in Detail Our side will form a joint committee to jointly preside over the inspection matters of the Shanghai concession factory inspection rights. Mayor Wu and Luo Shi and Chen, etc. are discussing in detail.

The proof method should be proposed by this chamber of commerce for each batch of transported Soviet rice. Father Sues Son for Unfilial Conduct, Appealing the Case 160

| The Judge Intended to Reconcile |

Wu Shaoqin of Datuan, Pudong, previously sued his biological son, Wu Daonan, in the Nanhui County Government for unfilial and violent conduct, stabbing his right arm with a knife, nearly resulting in an accident. The County Government verified the injury marks, and as a result, Wu Daonan was declared not guilty. Wu Shaoqin refused to accept the judgment and hired lawyers Yao Yuanding and Wang Fushang to file an appeal with the Shanghai District Court. The case was heard yesterday morning in the First Tribunal by Judge Guan Liting. The appellant, Wu Shaoqin, arrived in court with lawyer Wang, while Wu Daonan arrived with lawyer Pan Cheng'e, whom he had hired to defend him. Wu Shaoqin first stated that he was 44 years old, from Nanhui, and lived in Datuan Town. He was practicing medicine in the French Concession of Shanghai. The judge asked why he did not accept the judgment of Nanhui County. He replied that Wu Daonan was his biological son, born to his first wife, Jiang. Because Jiang had an affair with a man named Chen from Yangsiqiao, Daonan, under the instigation of his mother, attempted to murder him. The judge asked if he and Jiang lived in separate places. He replied that yes, he worked in Shanghai, so he lived in Shanghai with his later wife, Xiao, while Jiang lived at home in Datuan, Pudong. The judge asked when he married Xiao. He replied that he married her in the fourth year of the Republic of China. Because he returned home less often, Jiang took the opportunity to move to her mother's home in Lujiahui in the tenth year of the Republic of China. Jiang Yansheng was his father-in-law. Soon after, Jiang moved to Yangsiqiao and had an affair with Chen, who was very influential in the area. The judge asked if he sent money home. He replied that yes, and there was also rent to be collected at home. He had sued Jiang for cohabitation and had accused her of adultery in the court. On September 16 of last year, he returned home because his mother was ill. In the afternoon, in the evening, he was stabbed in the right arm by Daonan with a knife while sitting on a rattan chair in the厢房. He chased after Daonan and caught him. His mother died on the 21st of that month. The judge asked if there was any evidence. He replied that there was bloody clothing and the murder weapon. The judge then ordered Wu Daonan to the case. Daonan stated that he was 22 years old, lived in Yangsiqiao, and was in the flower factory business. Wu Shaoqin was his father. The judge asked why he murdered his father. He replied that he had not. On September 14 of last year, a relative named Tao said that his grandmother was ill. On the afternoon of the 15th, at 4 or 5 o'clock, he took advantage of the small break to go home. Because his father and mother had previously been involved in a lawsuit, he lived with his mother in Yangsiqiao, so his father was very dissatisfied with him. He saw his father when he returned home. He called him "Daddy," but his father did not respond and instead hit him. He then went to Tao's house to spend the night. On the 16th, he was arrested at the wheel port and taken to the bureau. The judge obtained the confession and said to Wu Shaoqin that you two do not need to litigate. Wu replied that he requested justice. The judge then said to Wu Daonan that you should apologize to your father. This case must be reconciled. As a result, the judge ordered a hearing to be scheduled at a later date.

| Shape Similar to an Old Ragpicker |

Hongchang Refrigeration Company

Refusing to Store Enemy Goods: Fresh Fish 167

Jiang Azhen Attempts Deception

Tu Wenzhao Righteously Refuses

Fresh fish, chicken, duck, and other such items must be sold on the same day. If stored for too long, the color and taste will change, and no one will buy them. Since the advent of refrigerated storage, fresh goods can be stored for one to two years without changing taste. Therefore, major restaurants and fresh goods stores must store large quantities of fresh goods every year to prevent shortages between seasons. Thus, refrigeration companies are an important part of the food market. Hongchang Refrigeration Company, located at 557 Miller Road, Hongkou, Shanghai, was established not long ago and has already gained a great reputation. On the 5th of this month, a person claiming to be Jiang Azhen brought a large quantity of fresh fish, requesting that the company refrigerate it. Little did they know that the fish were entirely enemy goods. The handler did not pay attention and was deceived into storing them. Tu Wenzhao, the manager of the company, is sharp and meticulous. Noticing that Jiang Azhen's attitude was unusual, he became suspicious. After investigating, he learned that all the goods were enemy goods. Manager Tu, filled with righteous indignation, immediately refused to store them and ordered Jiang to remove them immediately. Knowing that he could not continue the deception, Jiang loaded the fish and left. It is unknown what will happen to this large quantity of fresh enemy fish at the beginning of this hot season.

Luo Songshan, Utterly Desperate

Forging Champagne Tickets 169

Accomplice Qian Qingshan is 68 Years Old

Printed by Lu Quansheng's Printing House

Luo Songshan, a 34-year-old man from Zhenjiang, has recently been utterly desperate. Taking advantage of the spring horse racing season, he forged small champagne tickets and, on the 1st of this month, went to Wang Yunfang, his fellow townsman, at 88 North Suzhou Road to sell seven tickets for one yuan each, which he then spent. Luo thought that Wang did not recognize the genuine tickets, so he went to deceive him again on the 8th. However, Wang Yunfang had already found out. Just as he was about to negotiate with him, Luo walked right into the trap. Wang pretended to agree and secretly sent someone to report to the nearby No. 1073 Chinese constabulary. The constables arrested Luo and, upon searching him, Chinese detective Yang Zhaoqing found ten forged small champagne tickets and twenty-six yuan in cash. After questioning, it was learned that his accomplice was Qian Qingshan from Ningbo, 68 years old, who was hiding at 606 Tiantong Road. The detectives went and arrested Qian. They found five forged large champagne tickets worth ten yuan each in his room. It was learned that these forged tickets were manufactured by Lu Quansheng's printing house at 30 Beijing Road. They went to arrest Lu, but he had already fled after hearing the news. They confiscated a printing press and brought Qian Qingshan to the police station. The next morning, they were escorted to the summary court of the First Special District Court for questioning. The judge ordered them to be transferred to the local court for trial at a later date. This has already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan continued the hearing at the Third Criminal Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin presented the case, stating that this case was within the extended period. According to the defendant Luo Songshan, his friend Tang Jialin, who is on the run, sold as many as 90 of these forged champagne tickets. However, these forged tickets were all bought from Qian Qingshan, a total of one hundred tickets, purchased in two installments. The first time was on April 12th, when he bought fifty tickets, and the second time was on the 20th, when he bought another fifty tickets, paying one yuan and five jiao each time. The five forged large champagne tickets found in Qian Qingshan's possession were sent to the Shanghai Race Club, and Western staff member Litte examined them and found that they were indistinguishable from the real tickets, except for one different word in the Western text. According to Qian Qingshan, he had printed a total of one thousand of these small champagne tickets at Lu Quansheng's printing house on Beijing Road. He received them a month ago and distributed them with a Chen surname fugitive to Nanjing, Hangzhou, and other places. The number of people who were fooled by them is countless. The police station is now prosecuting them for fraud and obtaining property under Article 363 of the Criminal Law and for forging documents under Article 226. The forged champagne tickets and cash were presented for inspection. It was requested that they be severely prosecuted. When questioned, both defendants evaded the issue. Judge Wu ordered them to be remanded in custody for sentencing at a later date.

Gu Akun

Using a Cleaver to Kill His Own Daughter 170

And Kill His Niece Yang Acui

Heads Bleeding, Fortunately Not Dead

Gu Akun, a local, is 53 years old and works as a vendor. He lives at 199 Xundao Street, Dadongmen, Nanshi. However, Gu is addicted to opium and also likes to drink, so he often feels poor. Gu has a daughter named Jinfeng, who is 21 years old. Her mother died early, and she was raised by her father. She works as a yarn winder in a diligent sock factory in Huotui Lane, earning wages every month to supplement the family income. A few days ago, Gu took Jinfeng to the home of his brother-in-law, Mr. Yang, in Yangjia Town, Pudong, for several days. Gu returned home first, and Jinfeng, together with her cousin Yang Acui (20 years old), crossed the river to Nanshi at around 9:00 AM yesterday. Because Acui had been feeling abdominal pain recently, fearing that she had a disease, she went to see a doctor with Jinfeng for treatment. They returned home, and it was noon, so they had lunch together. At that time, Gu ordered Jinfeng to go to the street to buy wine for him, but Jinfeng refused. Gu became very angry and scolded her. Then, he angrily took a pot and went out to buy wine himself. After the meal, Jinfeng and Acui went to Xiaodongmen to buy patterns and then returned home. Gu had already drunk a lot of sorghum wine, his face red, his breath reeking of alcohol. Acui, because it was already past 3:00 PM, feared that her family would be waiting for her, so she bid farewell to her uncle (Gu Akun). Gu replied that it was still early, play for a while longer, don't worry, your uncle won't eat you. So, although Acui bid farewell repeatedly, she was not allowed to leave, so she sat on the bed and chatted with Jinfeng. Unexpectedly, not long after, Gu suddenly came from the kitchen, holding a cleaver, rushed into the room, tightly closed the door, and then raised the knife and first struck Jinfeng's head twice, and then struck Acui's head once. Both of them suffered serious head injuries. In an instant, blood flowed freely. They rushed out of the room, screaming for help. Wang Xingyi, the patrol officer in the area, heard the screams and rushed over. He saw that Jinfeng and Acui were both covered in blood, and Gu's head was also slightly injured, with blood flowing. He took all three of them to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, and then took them to the First Section of the First District, where Director Jin preliminarily questioned them. First, Yang Acui testified that she was inexplicably murdered by her uncle. Gu Jinfeng testified that she worked in a sock factory, and because her father's monthly income was very small, not enough for him to smoke, drink, and pay for all the household expenses, he often scolded and beat her. At lunch today, her father ordered her to go out and buy wine, and because the wine she usually bought for him was always called "fire wine" and not genuine sorghum, he often scolded her. Therefore, she did not agree to buy wine for her father today, and he held a grudge. Later, she and her cousin Acui returned from Xiaodongmen, and he used a knife to murder them. As for the minor injury to his head, he used the knife to cut himself. Gu Akun testified that Wang Gengsheng lived in the back building of his house. He used to work in a rubber shoe factory. Last year, he suddenly became intimate with his daughter Jinfeng. Because family scandals should not be spread, he endured it. Later, because Jinfeng was passionate about her affair, she asked to bring Wang home, but he firmly refused. Jinfeng regarded him as a thorn in her side and repeatedly discussed wanting to murder him. Today, Jinfeng gathered many people and used a cleaver to injure his head. He requested a thorough investigation. The director questioned him that Acui had no grievances or hatred with him, so how did she suffer such a serious head injury? Gu was speechless. Because he was drunk, he used a knife to injure his own daughter and niece, but still wanted to find excuses to blame others. He was ordered to prepare a document to be sent to the bureau for interrogation.

Inspection of Cured Ham 172

Executive Yuan Order Stresses Simplicity

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's inspection of cured ham has aroused opposition from the industry, and they have petitioned the Executive Yuan to stop it. According to the Executive Yuan's reply, in order to alleviate business difficulties, the inspection fee will be reduced. Later, due to the Municipal Health Bureau's detention of goods, the industry association and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce again petitioned the Executive Yuan. The Executive Yuan ordered the Municipal Government to strive for simplicity in the inspection procedures, in line with the purpose of inspection being to protect businesses. In addition to replying to the Executive Yuan, the Municipal Government also ordered the Municipal Health Bureau to comply. The original order of the Executive Yuan is transcribed below: Order for implementation. According to the report of the Ministry of Industry, the Shanghai Cured Ham Industry Association has petitioned to stop the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's inspection of cured ham, and it has been approved that the inspection fee should be reduced to show consideration. In addition to ordering the Shanghai Municipal Government to comply, the Ministry should be notified. I have received this. I secretly investigated that this case had previously been repeatedly petitioned by the industry association to cancel the inspection in order to alleviate business difficulties. Following the order, it should be temporarily allowed to be handled. It was originally expected that this case could be temporarily concluded, and a fundamental solution would be made when the internal sales inspection method was drafted. Later, due to the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's detention of goods and refusal to release them, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the industry association successively petitioned, detailing excessive fees, detention and harassment, and various other reasons, requesting that it be stopped in accordance with the law. While the matter was being carefully reviewed, it was ordered that the fee rate had been reduced, which showed the Executive Yuan's consideration of business difficulties. However, the original report mentioned more than just excessive fees. According to the order No. 23 of the National Government Jingzi of October last year, based on the original proposal of the Legislative Yuan, although the Ministry can formulate inspection methods for domestic goods separately, it also included the words "still must be based on not harming businesses or disturbing the people." The inspection of goods is originally to guarantee the quality of goods, thereby increasing credit and maintaining sales. Not only should the inspection fee be reduced as much as possible, but the inspection procedures should also be as simple as possible, in line with the purpose of inspection being to protect businesses. Now that the fee rate has been reduced, it seems necessary to strive for speed and convenience for businesses and the people in the inspection procedures. I hereby submit a document to request approval and order the Shanghai Municipal Government to transfer the order to the Health Bureau to strive for simplicity in the inspection procedures, paying special attention to it to show consideration. In addition to the instructions, the order is hereby given to the Municipal Government to immediately transfer the order to the Health Bureau to strive for simplicity in the inspection procedures to alleviate business difficulties. This order.

Murderer Wang Qiugen

Sentenced to Life Imprisonment 173

Cao Ajian, a carpenter, was lured to the vicinity of the Siming Guild Hall in Pudong at around 7:00 PM on April 15th last year by Zhou Axiang, Zhou Jinshan, Wang Qiugen, and others, and was axed to death. The case was discovered two weeks later, and the perpetrators had fled without a trace. Only the suspect Wang Qiugen was arrested. After repeated investigations and clear confirmation by the Criminal Court of the District Court, it was proven that Zhou Axiang initiated the crime together with his younger brother Zhou Jinshan and Wang Qiugen. The debate was considered concluded, awaiting sentencing. The details have been reported in the previous newspaper. It is now known that the case was sentenced yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM by Judge Luo Renji, who ordered Wang Qiugen to be brought to the case and questioned briefly before announcing the sentence in court. Wang Qiugen was sentenced to life imprisonment for the crime of murder. After the sentence was announced, he was ordered to be returned to custody, awaiting the expiration of the appeal period before being sent to prison.

Park Conditions in April 174

The report of the Chief of Parks of the Public Works Department states that in April, the walkway from Zhaofeng Park to the zoo has been widened, and a portion of the strange stone walkway in the flowing water garden has been renovated. Bulbous flowers are now in full bloom. In the zoo, three pheasant cages have been added, and a new enclosure has been built for the newly arrived Malayan otter. In addition, a wild cat and a parrot have arrived. The summer sports fields in Hongkou and Huishan Parks have been allocated. Hongkou Park has fifty-five grass tennis courts, five hard-surface tennis courts, four grass ball fields, and one baseball field. Huishan Park has seven grass tennis courts and one grass ball field. They are used by various sports groups. The seats in the parks have been repaired and repainted. The summer huts have been re-covered, and a portion of the park fences has been renovated. The number of visitors to Zhaofeng Park this month totaled 134,731, including 85,886 season ticket holders, 16,907 ticket purchasers, and 31,938 children. The highest number of visitors in April in previous years was 82,333 in 1931. This year's number exceeds that by more than 50,000. Including other parks, the total number of visitors in April reached 259,168.

Russian Tea Specialist in China

Budget for Purchasing Chinese Tea Quantities 177

To be Completed in Two Weeks and Reported to the Russian Government

International Trade Bureau Collects Tea Samples

Ji Zejin, Director and Secretary of the Guidance Office of the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, said yesterday that the quantity of Chinese tea sold to Russia has been greatly reduced to 3 million taels last year due to the influence of Indian and Japanese tea. Tea merchants have requested assistance from both the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry. Now, efforts are being made to negotiate with both the silver and money industries. Russia's import and export goods are all state-owned. For the tea trade with China, India, and Japan, a specialist has been sent to handle it. The specialist in China is Mr. Bekoff. He is now in Shanghai. At the time when new tea is on the market, the specialist has begun to investigate the selling price and supply and demand situation of tea in Shanghai, and whether Chinese tea can be sold on credit until December before payment. He plans to draft a detailed budget and report it to the Moscow Russian government within two weeks, and then decide on the purchase quantity. If we cannot sell tea to Russia on credit at the time of this tea decline, the amount of tea sold to Russia will probably be greatly reduced again. Ji also told reporters that the bureau previously convened a meeting of tea merchants to discuss relief measures, and decided on one item, which was to collect various samples of tea produced in China and send them to our consulates in major cities of various countries for exhibition and publicity, so as to implement direct trade between tea merchants and tea-buying countries. The bureau has now collected dozens of types and will soon be able to complete them and send them to various countries. (Daily News)

Wusong District

Construction of Health Office Begins 180

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau originally had a health district office in Wusong. Due to the January 28th Incident, the office was located in a war zone, so all work was completely destroyed. Since Li Ting'an took over as Director of the Municipal Health Bureau in January last year, in view of the importance of this cause to the interests of the local people, he has made every effort to restore it. The original Haibin Hospital in Wusong, which was run by local charities, was also completely destroyed during the war and unable to be restored. Therefore, Director Li sent personnel to consult with the Wusong Jide Hall to rent the site of the Haibin Hospital at a very low rental price to build the Wusong District Health Office, in order to promote health care, treatment, disease prevention, maternity protection, and health education. On the one hand, Director Li planned the funding and requested that the Post-War Rehabilitation Committee decide to subsidize 32,000 yuan. The Ministry of Health of the Ministry of Interior allocated 5,073 yuan, 1 jiao, and 6 fen. The National Tongji University proposed cooperation to facilitate internships for the Department of Public Health of the university. After both parties negotiated, they have actively started construction. Bids for the construction of the office building will begin immediately, and it is expected to be completed within a few months. This is good news for the health prospects of the local citizens.

Publishing World 187

▲ Post-War European Economic History

The Commercial Press has recently published "Post-War European Economic History," originally titled "A History of Recent European Economic Development," written by Professor Ogg of the University of Wisconsin, USA. In 1924, it was translated by Li Guangzhong and entrusted to the Press for publication, and it was quite popular at the time. However, Li's translation was based on the 1916 edition, and the materials covered only went up to 1914. The wartime and post-war situations were not described. Therefore, Dr. Schap, in 1926, compiled six chapters systematically on the economic situation in Europe during the ten years after the war, such as population, land, food, agriculture, industry, commerce, shipping, labor, and finance, and appended them to the original book as a supplement. The edition now published by the Press is the translation of this supplement. The book is rich in information and detailed in its descriptions and is undoubtedly a famous work on modern economics. Although the materials in it do not include the most recent years' economic situation, many of today's world economic events are rooted in the impact of the Great War. Therefore, studying this book will make it easier to understand the causes and consequences of recent economic changes. Moreover, our country's economy is backward, and everything needs to be rebuilt. This book can especially serve as a reference. The book is translated by Lin Guangcheng, the writing style is clear and fluent, and the printing and binding are also excellent.

Mr. Wang Zhaoshi's Views on the Future of Sino-Japanese Relations during National Humiliation Memorial Week 192

Speech at the YMCA on May 10th

Gentlemen, I believe everyone has an urgent question in their minds today that needs answering. That is: will Japan continue its aggression, or will it be satisfied with just seizing the three northeastern provinces and Jehol? You may recall that when Shenyang fell during the "September 18th Incident," some complacent and short-sighted people believed that the problem would not escalate. Later, when northern Manchuria and Jinzhou were lost, these complacent and short-sighted people again thought that Japan would be satisfied with just seizing the three northeastern provinces and that it would not escalate further. Then, when Shanhaiguan was lost, these complacent and short-sighted people again believed that Japan had seized Shanhaiguan and could ensure the security of the "Manchukuo puppet state" and would be satisfied with that, without escalating further. But then Jehol was lost. These complacent and short-sighted people again thought that Japan had seized Jehol and completed the natural terrain of the "Manchukuo puppet state" and would certainly not escalate further, and certainly not expand within the Great Wall. But now, most of Chahar has already been lost, and eastern Luanda has also been lost. These complacent and short-sighted people are still dreaming, thinking that Japan will never attack Tianjin and Peiping.

Since the "September 18th Incident," I have not dared to dream. I am even less willing to bury my head in the sand, pretending not to see the danger, like an ostrich. I believe that Japan will continue its aggression without end. There are three reasons for this: (1) Territorial connection. Japan has seized the three northeastern provinces and Jehol and will inevitably advance southward, like the westward expansion movement of the United States, which did not stop until it spanned the entire continent to the Pacific coast. Japan will eventually sweep across our entire country. This is Tanaka's policy, and it is also a natural trend. In the eyes of the Japanese, it will be realized sooner or later. (2) Ensuring the security of the acquired land. Japan will inevitably take offense as the best form of defense. After gaining the Northeast, it will invade North China to use North China as a buffer zone. After gaining North China, it will invade the Yangtze River basin to use the Yangtze River basin as a buffer zone. After gaining the Yangtze River basin, it will invade South China. Only after conquering our entire country will Japan be satisfied and sleep soundly. (3) Although a world war will not happen immediately, it will be difficult to avoid in the future. Japan knows that it is the culprit in the Far East and cannot help but actively prepare. Since the country is small and poor in resources, it must use China as its base for militaristic expansion.

Will Japan's continuous aggression policy succeed? It depends on three aspects: (1) Whether the international community will actively intervene in Japan's actions. Everyone knows that this is a period of global economic crisis. The United Kingdom and the United States are busy reorganizing internally. Since Hitler came to power in Germany, the atmosphere in Europe has been unusually tense. Furthermore, the people of various countries have not been far removed from the European war, and everyone is unwilling to have a second world war occur immediately. As for Soviet Russia, firstly because the national foundation is not strong, and secondly because the five-year plan has not been completed, it not only cannot support weak nations, but recently it has colluded with our enemies, despised our national sovereignty, and sold the China Eastern Railway to the "Manchukuo puppet state." Therefore, in the current international situation, the international community will not actively intervene in Japan's actions. Japan can continue its aggression without fear. (2) Whether internal strife or revolution will occur within Japan. If internal strife or revolution occurs, it can restrain Japan's aggressive behavior. In the eyes of complacent and enslaved Chinese people, this is something they pray for day and night. But with Japan's China policy going smoothly and unstoppable, the general Japanese public is overjoyed and celebrating. Where would there be any revolution? Only when China encounters strong resistance, fails militarily, the scope of the war expands, and the burden on the people increases, will the people turn from dissatisfaction and disappointment to revolution, like Germany in the European war. If France was the China of today, and simply did not resist, then the German Empire would not only not have had a revolution, but its foundation would be even more solid. (3) Whether China resists or not. We all know that even if there is resistance, it is only local resistance, stemming from the patriotic zeal of local military officers. But the more China does not resist, the more Japan advances. The more Japan advances, the more China does not resist. As a result, in a year and a half, carelessly, half of the country will be lost. Conversely, if we had desperately resisted from the beginning, Japan's aggressive policy would not have been so smooth, and it would not have been so rapid. The reason it continues to be so rapid is precisely because we continue to retreat so rapidly.

But the government still says that it is a long-term resistance. For example, not long ago, Premier Wang Jingwei specifically issued a very long telegram to explain the issue of war and peace, saying, "Because we cannot fight, we resist. Because we cannot make peace, we negotiate. Therefore, resistance and negotiation proceed simultaneously." But we must ask, is what is called war military conflict? If we use military force to resist, is that war? Wasn't the resistance of the 19th Route Army in Shanghai war? Wasn't the resistance of Song Zheyuan's army at Xifengkou war? Wasn't the resistance of Xu Tingyao's army at Gubeikou war? If what Mr. Wang calls resistance is not military resistance, but resistance that dares not fight, then what is the difference between this and Mr. Zhang Xueliang's non-resistance policy? As for "Because we cannot make peace, we negotiate," we understand even less why we should negotiate with Japan, knowing that we cannot make peace. Does negotiation mean hoping for peace? The result of the government's "two-faced policy" (resisting on one hand and negotiating on the other) is that not only is the government indecisive, unable to grasp the direction, and without a plan, but even we ordinary people do not know what to do.

Free Talk

On "Integrity" 193

Walking past the foreign barracks on ××× Road, I encountered this incident. A short, fat officer came out, and five or six rickshaws across the street rushed towards him all at once. The swift-footed got there first, and two rickshaws had already stopped at his feet. Perhaps because he saw that the cushion of the second rickshaw was a bit whiter, the short, fat man retracted his right foot, which had already stepped onto the first rickshaw, and jumped onto the second. The first rickshaw puller seemed unwilling to give up, grabbing the handlebar of the second rickshaw. The result: he was kicked by the short, fat man.

Two gentlemen in brand-new "spring attire" walking in front of me began to comment.

"Really asking for trouble!" one said.

"These rickshaw pullers always rush to pull foreigners, they deserve to be beaten. They think foreigners will give more money丨Really lack integrity丨Really lack integrity丨" The other seemed even more indignant, saying "Really lack integrity" twice in a row.

I shuddered.

He actually demanded "integrity" from the rickshaw pullers! A certain celebrity who doesn't ride in rickshaws for "humanitarian" reasons (mentioning him reminds me of his two famous sayings: Soviet Russian ugly species, Jewish beast species. But this kind of voice seems to have disappeared now!) I've long heard his name: but demanding "integrity" from rickshaw pullers is a first for me. I think most gentlemen share the same opinion.

My point is not that rickshaw pullers shouldn't have integrity. But in this society where the comprador bourgeoisie rules everything, and all the high-ranking Chinese, scholars, and gentlemen are docile citizens and loyal dogs, this precious man is resentful of the rickshaw pullers' lack of integrity. I can't help but shudder. A rickshaw costs more than ten 角 in rental fees a day. The puller probably has a wife and children at home to support. He can't afford much "integrity" in order to pull a few more coins. If a certain celebrity changed his "not riding in rickshaws" to "giving rickshaw pullers more money," it might be more "humanitarian."

In fact, this thing called integrity seems to have long been extinct among the higher-ranking Chinese. On the other hand, it still exists a little bit among the lower classes like rickshaw pullers. For example, they know how to hate. If you have seen the expression on the face of the rickshaw puller mentioned above after being kicked, seen the way the pullers curse the police with gritted teeth, you will know what I mean by hate. As for the higher-ranking Chinese, they can only be docile citizens and dogs.

Rain 194

— Lin Huiyin

Although I lay in bed, I just couldn't sleep. When my thoughts were interrupted, I would hear the combined melody of the clock and the rain. Seeing the first light of day already squeezing in from the rain, I felt especially troubled. Seeing that I wouldn't be able to sleep, I simply got up.

It felt like I had a lot to talk about with someone, and then someone I could talk to entered my heart. So I decided to go find that person who had entered my heart.

He, the person who had entered my heart, lived in a village about forty minutes by train from the city, in a school. When the train arrived there, the rain wasn't very heavy. I didn't want to take a rickshaw, so I followed the road signs towards the school. But by the time I got to the school, my hat was soaked through, dripping water erratically. It was too embarrassing, as if I deliberately wanted to make the host look difficult. I felt a little uneasy.

Good, he wasn't at the school. They said he lived in the city and wouldn't have class until the afternoon, and asked me to either wait there or come back later. I didn't feel disappointed, but surprised, because I didn't expect him to not be there. Although, at this point, it seemed like I didn't necessarily have to see him. Because the things I wanted to talk to him about had completely disappeared in the vast rain. I wanted to return to the city, but the train wasn't for another hour and a half, so I went to a public tea house near the station to drink tea.

The tea house faced a small river, with a wooden bridge at the end of the river. Not far from the bridge were two or three sailboats. And, as if to accompany my loneliness, the rain continued to fall. The rain, the river, the bridge, the boats, congealed into a reversing car, sending me into the fourteenth and fifteenth centuries. I sat on a long bench less than five inches wide, gazing at everything selflessly.

Hongkou Park 195

— Ma Guoliang

I don't usually like to go anywhere, but a foot ailment for a month has forced me to stay indoors all day, making me envious of those who can move freely. The day my foot got better was a Sunday, and the weather was so nice, so I went to nearby Hongkou Park by myself.

I hadn't been to Hongkou Park since the January 28th Incident. Many friends haven't been either, supposedly because there are too many Japanese people inside. However, I don't think that should be a reason not to go.

This is our land too. Why shouldn't we be happy to go to our own land?

After paying twenty cents, I was allowed to enter the "public" park, pacing alone on the cinder path, crossing the wooden bridge, walking on the grass, resting on the stones, and squatting by the stream. Even though I was alone, it had a different kind of fun. Looking here, running there, regarding others as scenery or a play, it's enough to keep you from feeling lonely.

Since the weather was good, there were many visitors, needless to say. Red, green, black, and white, all people, appearing and disappearing by the stream, by the trees, on the chairs, and on the grass. Among them, there were Westerners, Easterners, white people, yellow people, brown people... all kinds. Naturally, the most were our compatriots and the Japanese people seen every day in Hongkou.

There were all sorts of scenes. Two Westerners, perhaps debating the Sino-Japanese issue, were arguing red-faced. Two Indian women and a man with a white turban were flirting, entangled for a long time without any resolution. Japanese children were running around with sun flags, while Chinese children always hid beside their mothers or fathers. Japanese people were playing ball and fishing; Chinese people were smoking, strolling, chatting, and practicing Tai Chi.

This place is a paradise; people are all well-dressed, displaying a leisurely demeanor. With their bellies full, they come here for a walk to aid digestion, which is naturally necessary.

Here, there is no "world economic panic," no "outbreak of World War II," no "efforts to assist front-line soldiers," no "killing all the Japanese devils." Chinese people, Japanese people, everyone is smiling, not glaring at each other.

Therefore, this place can also be said to be Sino-Japanese amity, coexistence and co-prosperity, and even a world "already" advanced to Great Harmony.

After walking for a long time, I finally found a chair by the pond. Just as I sat down, I saw on the opposite bank, on a narrow path, a Chinese family and a Japanese family walking towards each other. They were all politely stepping aside to give way to each other. I couldn't help but sigh that Sino-Japanese relations were indeed amicable, and the world had indeed achieved Great Harmony! Fortunately, I hadn't even brought a newspaper to the park to read today, otherwise, if I had seen it writing about the fierce battles between the Chinese and Japanese in the Luan River, I would have definitely cursed the journalists for lying.

If the journalists weren't lying, and the Chinese and Japanese soldiers were really still fighting there; if we had the chance to tell a Japanese soldier that while he was risking his life on the battlefield, his compatriots were fishing in a park in our country. Who do you think he would aim his gun at when he heard that?

I remember seeing a cartoon by an American cartoonist with the caption: "War is encouraged by people who don't go to war... while people who don't want to go to war are forced to fight!" The cause and effect of wars throughout history have been mostly like this, and it's not unique to Japan!

As I walked out of the gate of this paradise of Great Harmony, I was immediately greeted by the grand Japanese barracks under construction, and passing in front of it were the Chinese Boy Scouts collecting donations for national aviation defense.

Airplane vs. Snail Race 196

— Ke Duo

In the world today, this "mysterious" country, the Soviet Union, has many unique things that people have never heard of or seen. Since implementing the Five-Year Economic Plan in 1928, it has implemented a unique and comical competition: an airplane vs. a snail race. Hearing this for the first time, one must find it very strange. In fact, the Soviet Union is not truly conducting an airplane vs. snail race; this is just a sign of the achievements of Socialist Competition.

What is Socialist Competition? This is Lenin's legacy. He said: "Socialism does not eliminate competition; on the contrary, it expands competition on the basis of the masses, so that the working masses can truly develop their talents. In today's implementation of socialism, our task is to organize this competition." This competition has now become widespread in all institutions throughout the Soviet Union: between industrial enterprises, between workshops within enterprises, between shock brigades (Shock Brigade丨a new type of physical labor organization founded by 120 young female workers at the "Red Triangle" factory in Leningrad in September 1926, which became a mass movement throughout the country by 1929), between individual workers, between industrial enterprises and agriculture, between state farms, between collective farms, and even between Soviets, armies, schools, hospitals, and nurseries and kindergartens.

The method of competition is that a certain workshop, enterprise, or state farm, proposes competition items to its counterpart in the same category, or to other appropriate counterparts. Both parties sign a contract and begin to implement the competition. A review committee determines the winner, and models such as airplanes, cars, streetcars, bicycles, turtles, and snails are used as symbols of the competition results. Those with excellent work have their factory names written on airplanes and cars, and are given prizes to show encouragement; those with poor work have their factory names written on turtles and snails, as a mark of shame.

What is the result of implementing Socialist Competition? The result is: the Five-Year Economic Plan was completed in four years. In the industrial sector, production plans were completed and exceeded predetermined figures, production costs were reduced, labor productivity was increased, production quality was improved, absenteeism and sabotage were reduced, and incidental expenses were reduced. In the agricultural sector, sown areas were expanded, farming methods were improved, rural electrification was accelerated, and wealthy peasants were eliminated. In various institutions, staff members worked quickly, and bureaucrats were purged.

Carrot Top 197

— Jules Kenaru, translated by Lin Quzuo

The Blind Man

He gently tapped the door with the end of his cane.

"It's Repic's house 丨 what's he here for again, that fellow?"

"Repic 丨 Don't you know? He's here to get his six sous; it's the day he comes to collect his money. Let him in."

Repic's wife reluctantly ran to open the door, and because it was very cold outside, she grabbed the blind man's hand and dragged him inside roughly.

"Good morning, everyone!" said the blind man.

He walked inside. His cane moved slowly on the paved stone floor, as if chasing mice, until it encountered a chair. The blind man sat down and stretched his frozen hands towards the stove.

Repic took out a six-sous coin and said:

"Take it!"

Then he ignored him and continued to read his newspaper.

Carrot Top was playing. He squatted in a corner, watching the blind man's wooden shoes: the snow on the shoes was melting, and small streams of water were already visible around them.

Repic's wife saw it.

"Lend me your wooden shoes, old man," she said.

She took the wooden shoes and placed them under the fireplace, but it was too late; a mess of water had already been left on the floor. Feeling uneasy, the blind man's feet felt wet, and he kept lifting one foot and then the other, trying to get away from the muddy snow water, which only made the snow water spread further.

Carrot Top scratched the ground with his fingernails, as if pointing out the deeper cracks to the dirty water, calling it to flow towards him. "Since he's already got his six sous, what's he still sitting here for?" said Repic's wife, regardless of whether the blind man could hear her.

But the blind man was talking politics, at first hesitantly, but later more fluently. Sometimes when he finished speaking, he would wave his cane, hitting his fist on the stove's chimney, scalding himself. He quickly withdrew it, with a look of doubt on his face, his white eyeballs rolling in his tearful eyes.

Sometimes Repic would turn the newspaper over and say:

"That's right, Daddy Dixier, that's right, but do you think this matter is reliable?"

"You ask me if I think this matter is reliable!" the blind man shouted. "Ah, so such a thing has happened, that's too serious! Listen to me, Mr. Repic, let me tell you how I became blind."

"He's not going to leave," said Repic's wife.

Indeed, the blind man felt better here than outside. He recounted his accidental encounter, stretching his limbs, his whole body melting. Some ice cubes were melting in his veins, flowing along. His clothes and limbs seemed to be dripping with oil. The puddle of muddy water on the floor gradually increased, flowing towards Carrot Top, already reaching his side.

Carrot Top was the target of this muddy water flow.

Soon he would be able to play with this muddy water. (To be continued)
