Spring and Autumn

Two Kinds of Thoughts 273

— Zhanlu

Virtuous Mothers and Good Wives versus Glamorous Mothers and Bright Wives

The most dangerous great man is undoubtedly Gandhi; does China have a great man like Gandhi? No. China's great men are proponents of suffering, not Gandhians. I remember a certain great man saying, "A miserable Chinese person," which was simply lamenting the suffering of the Chinese people, advocating a kind of suffering. However, if everyone embraces suffering, there is a possibility of hardship turning into happiness. Unfortunately, in war-torn areas, everyone embraces suffering; in places of ease, everyone embraces hedonism. The suffering suffer, and the joyful rejoice, which is why such a phenomenon arises.

Eastern women's education has not escaped the virtuous mother and good wife doctrine; some say that the virtuous mother and good wife doctrine is a form of slavery. Our Chinese women's education surpasses this doctrine, focusing not only on the four characters of virtuous mother and good wife. However, recent women's education often neglects virtuous mothers and good wives, focusing instead on glamorous mothers and bright wives, which sound similar but have different meanings. Clearly having become a mother, the child is handed over to a nanny to manage, while the mother dresses brightly and goes to the dance floor, which is the glamorous mother doctrine. Clearly having become a housewife, she manages nothing, focusing only on beauty; clothing, food, housing, and transportation are all about beauty. She only hopes that people will praise her as a "beautiful lady," which brings her more satisfaction than being called a "greatly virtuous lady," which is called the bright wife doctrine.

Rendering Them Incapable of Bearing Children 274

— Lily

A few days ago, all the newspapers published "news" from Germany stating that, in order to improve the race, the National Socialist Party would enact new laws to render criminals and those who are physically or mentally unsound incapable of bearing children.

As for what "incapable of bearing children" actually means, the telegram was too brief, and we are not able to guess. I imagine there will be an explanation next time.

In the houses of our country's emperors, the thirty-six palaces and seventy-two courtyards housed countless "imperial concubines" who "never had the emperor's favor in their lives." Therefore, all male servants on duty in the palace had their "things" cut off to prevent dry firewood from meeting a raging fire. These "disempowered" friends are called eunuchs. I don't know if Germany wants to "render them incapable of bearing children" by adopting this foolproof, humane, and fundamentally resolving "castration" method.

I really don't know if it's a coincidence, or if the Germans are imitating Eastern civilization. Because in Chinese history, there was a lowly historian who wrote good articles, but angered an unprogressive emperor who loved flattery and hated criticism, who, like the Germans, "rendered him incapable of bearing children," to prevent the "dragons begetting dragons, phoenixes begetting phoenixes, and thieves raising sons to dig holes in the walls" from passing on an unambiguous little Sima Qian to stir things up.

If this law is ever implemented, then prisoners released from prison and patients in hospitals will each be "doomed." From then on, in Berlin, "eunuchs will walk the streets," which is good for wanting children. From then on, "sitting still without being tempted" cannot be monopolized by Liu Xiahui.

Food and sex are human nature. Women and bread are equally important in life. Everyone is afraid of this move, so they are cautious and dare not engage in activities that violate criminal law or harm health. This is the great principle of improving the race. To put it plainly, for example, "spitting anywhere" and "urinating anywhere" will "render them incapable of bearing children," then who would dare to "spit anywhere" or "urinate anywhere"? Who would associate "Chinese people" with "dogs"?

Some are worried that China will follow suit. I say, rest assured, China already has people planning to solve the sexual desires of prisoners.

Gold Exchange Sketch 275

— Huang Kewei

By the Huangpu River, at the intersection of Jiujiang Road. Under the pressure of the great banks of Citibank and Mitsui, the Gold Exchange bows its head and gasps for breath!

Here, there is no clean, harmonious air, only a chaotic, terrifying, and stimulating din. When the Jianghai Customs clock strikes nine, this dry market begins to fill with emaciated figures dressed in tattered clothes and shoes. But there are also a few big shots who have not yet been drained of blood, standing like Buddhas, stretching out their arms, gesturing, and shouting: "Buy in at × yuan, sell out at × yuan."

The red lights reporting market prices rotate like a revolving lantern, and the customers sitting on high stools follow the red lights with their big pupils. Their faces constantly display strange expressions of joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness. If they were filmed at that time, it would be a giant comedy. 丨丨Big news, silver prices soar. 丨丨Draft, the shilling fluctuates. 丨丨Large holders of long positions emerge. 丨丨People's hearts are down, and standard gold plunges. Those with long positions laugh until their stomachs hurt, and Western-style houses, cars, and concubines are turning before their eyes. Those with short positions see the blood-red headlines in the newspaper: 丨丨Standard gold plummets by sixty-five yuan and five jiao. They rush out the door, take a sampan, cross to the center of the river, jump into the rapid current, and go to the river house to dream of their golden money!

Dregs 276

— Yan Chonglou

People's thoughts are created by the environment, and people's actions are prompted by thoughts.

○ ○ ○

One thinks one is making a precise choice, but sometimes one chooses the worst one!

○ ○ ○

Fatigue? The poor are fatigued by work. The rich are fatigued by games.

○ ○ ○

Objects placed in the open will exist safely, but objects hidden in the dark will disappear without a trace.

○ ○ ○

Thieves are often crushed under the law, while big robbers often roam outside the bounds of the law.

○ ○ ○

"Something you don't want to do, but you can't not do." This is the characteristic of modernity.

○ ○ ○

"Luck" and "misfortune" are connected. If you harbor "luck," you will get "misfortune"!

○ ○ ○

There are two kinds of opposite liquids in the world: "the tears of the weak," and "the blood of the strong."

Long Novel

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 277

— Zhang Changshui

Chapter Seven: Severing Affection with a Few Words and Weeping Behind Closed Doors; Shouldering Righteousness and Discussing Over Wine

Gan Jizhi and the old maiden of the Yang family thought that this secret meeting in the milk tea shop was very safe, but unexpectedly, they ran into his elder brother Houzhi. Needless to say, the words he and the old maiden said were completely heard by his brother. Undoubtedly, his brother would definitely give him a big lesson. It's just that listening to this kind of lesson in a coffee shop, along with a group of onlookers, would make people laugh, and it would be embarrassing. For this reason, it was best to slip away, and when he got home, he would let his brother scold him as much as he wanted. Thinking this way, he didn't care what his brother looked like, rushed to pay for the refreshments at the milk tea shop, lowered his head, and went home. When he got home, he slipped into the study, his heart still pounding. He thought to himself that he must not let his brother get too angry, and when his brother said something, he would admit his mistake. He sat listlessly at the table, holding his head in his hands, just thinking about how to calm his brother's anger, what his brother would say, and how he would admit his mistake? He was thinking like this. His mind was like fifteen buckets drawing water, fluctuating up and down, but Gan Houzhi did not regard this matter as an urgent official document, and did not return home until after nine o'clock in the evening. Jizhi was waiting for his brother's rebuke and hadn't slept yet. However, Houzhi returned to the main room and went directly to talk to his sister-in-law, and did not pay attention to this matter. Jizhi thought that his brother probably thought that they were both upright men and it was inconvenient to embarrass him too much, thinking that he had already decided not to say anything. This relieved him of some worries and he fell asleep peacefully. When he got up the next day, he still went to work as usual, feeling deeply lucky, thinking that he had already passed this difficult hurdle. However, a problem occurred when he came back this afternoon. The maid said that the lady wanted to talk to the second master in the main room. Hearing this, Jizhi knew that there was a reason and his heart pounded again. Madam Gan was sitting on a chair in the main room, holding a cigarette in her mouth, her mood very calm. Seeing Jizhi coming in, she smiled slightly at him. Jizhi stood at the door and said: "Sister-in-law, did you call me for something?" Madam Gan pointed to a chair opposite and said: "Sit down and talk slowly. What are you busy with?" (73)

On the Public Bus 278

— Ji Kan

Waiting, waiting. Several men at the bus stop, chewing cigars, looking at the advertisements in the newspapers: pacing leisurely, their attitude so idle and silent.

Two high-heeled leather shoes moved towards this side, and the bus stop was immediately like a flower bomb exploding. The elderly gentleman pulled at his collar, feeling uneasy as if he had a fever. The myopic Mr. Spectacles was looking at people with his forehead, while the one with the cane was desperately digging the ground.

Following, following, like food being loaded into a stall, I was stuffed into the public bus.

The young gentlemen sitting in the row of seats reserved for women, their attitude as solemn as if they were going to the office, but their eyes were secretly peeking at the bodies of those sitting next to them, as slippery as a thief.

Spitting out a few people, and swallowing a few more, the bus passed another stop. At the entrance and exit, a Chinese man in a blue cloth robe was stepped on his cloth-shoe foot by a well-dressed, high-class Chinese, and cried out in pain. It was so ungraceful that this high-class Chinese was startled, turned his head and gave him a hateful glare, and strode into the carriage.

A vase sat comfortably in the open seat at the rear of the bus, vibrating sharply and rhythmically with the sound of the bus. The vase's whole body was cramping, revealing some secrets of youth on its face.

A middle-aged man in a suit was spitting hard against the glass window; a foreign woman sitting to the right of the same row of seats quickly turned her head to the right, frowning, showing an ugly, contemptuous expression, as if she were saying to everyone in the car: "How annoying and dirty are the Chinese people with lung disease!"

World Rarities

Classification of Chinese Students in Paris 279

— Zhu Mei

Because I went to visit the University of Paris, a friend talked to me about the life of Chinese students. 丨丨I have mentioned it in the previous article, but not in detail丨丨China has greatly reduced its faith in overseas students recently. In the past, hearing that someone was an overseas student was like seeing a Westerner, and they were treated with respect. If they were said to be a foreign doctor, then twelve thousand points of admiration were added to the respect. Now, we are used to seeing overseas students, and it is still the same thing. The only difference is that they have eaten bread for a few years, or learned a little Western style. Otherwise, a rice bucket is still a rice bucket, and they are not necessarily better than domestic students. As for doctors, that is naturally another case of selling dog meat with a sheep's head. Some so-called doctors are often not as good as those without doctorates, so everyone is even less trusting of overseas students. However, we must first understand that overseas students are not some sacred thing. Overseas students are originally not as respected in other countries as they are in China. They are really very respected, and the reason for the respect is that their country does not easily let a student go to another country. That is, they must learn something and come back. (Their thoughts also have great differences) In addition, the economic and cultural conditions of various countries are different, which are naturally very different from China. As for China, to put it simply, the country has not thought about what overseas students will learn abroad to help China (you can tell from the fact that the diplomatic organs do not pay attention to the lives of overseas students), and the so-called overseas students are not all trying to get something by studying abroad. We can see this from the following classification of overseas students:

(1) Studying abroad for knowledge. The so-called knowledge includes everything, such as industry, culture, etc. This type of student generally accounts for the least number. Regarding their economy, some are completely poor. Some have very little funding.

(2) Studying abroad to retire. The so-called retirement should refer to big shots, but some small officials, after being politically defeated, cleverly scraped together some money and used studying abroad as an excuse to study abroad.

(3) Studying abroad for fun. There are many such people, such as some of those mentioned above who are studying abroad to retire. China is not short of children of bureaucrats or gentry, who feel that China is not fun, so they also come under the name of studying abroad.

(4) Studying abroad for fame. Such people generally admire overseas students themselves. They think that if they have money, they should also go abroad and come back with the sign of an overseas student.

(5) Studying abroad for no apparent reason. These people generally have not graduated from middle school, and they follow others to study abroad because others say so.

(6) Overseas students sent by the government. Most of these overseas students have been masters, and they are no longer completely students in thought and life. However, they come to foreign countries to experience the life of overseas students.

As for other reasons, there are many more. But we simply examine how many of these complex overseas students are actually studying? And if those overseas students who did not come to study return to do foolish things, can you not blame the overseas students for being bad? But you know that there are so many overseas students, 丨丨who can stop anyone from studying abroad if they have money丨丨You can also understand everything. Therefore, those who scold overseas students in China should understand this reason, and at the same time, please do not worship, whether they are doctors or not, Chinese students or foreign students, if they have no ability, just treat them the same!

Talk

Universal Remedy 280

— Tianfang

When you get sick, you must take medicine. This is probably an unchanging principle in ancient and modern times, both in China and abroad. Although things like colds do not necessarily require medication and can heal on their own, if the symptoms are a little more serious, or if you don't want to be bedridden for a long time, it is always advisable to take medicine, which even not very smart people can understand.

The difficulty arises when it comes to taking medicine. How many diseases are there in the world? You have to ask a doctor of medicine about this, but I am not a medical student, so I don't know the details. But since the Tang Dynasty, there have been more than 5,300 "Golden Prescriptions." If each prescription is only for treating one disease, then just in terms of "national diseases," there are at least half a million. Other diseases imported from foreign countries, such as "yellow fever" and "black death," are not included. The problem arises here: there are so many diseases, and I think even doctors may not be able to remember them completely clearly, so prescribing the right medicine is a bit of a hassle. And people like Bian Que and Hua Tuo are rarely seen these days, and news of quack doctors killing people is often seen in newspapers. It really makes sick people quite hesitant. Moreover, humans in the 20th century are used to living at high speeds, and who would bother to carefully examine and slowly treat? Therefore, a simple treatment method, 丨丨the invention of a universal remedy, is imminent. If the drugs for typhoid fever to venom, etc., can be steamed, distilled, squeezed, and fused into one dose according to the "sovereign, minister, assistant, and envoy" principles, like a palindrome poem, viewed horizontally or sideways, all can be used wonderfully. Even if there are tens of thousands of diseases, there is only one prescription, wouldn't it be a two-way benefit for the patient, the doctor, and the pharmacy? 丨丨Perhaps at that time, producers, 丨丨pharmacies, and consumers, 丨丨patients, will be able to trade directly, and doctors will not be needed, which is something that famous doctors of ancient times, such as Hua Tuo, did not expect.

The 20th century is said to be the era of Asia, so the honor of this invention falls on the Second Model Prison of Caohejing, Shanghai, Jiangsu Province, China. Because it is a "model," it houses a particularly large number of prisoners, accommodating more than 1,700 people. Recently, because it is not enough, they are discussing building a new prison.

Although prisoners have lost their physical freedom, their freedom to get sick has not been taken away along with it. 丨丨On the contrary, inside the iron windows, it is more suitable for getting sick. Most of the heroic young people, arrested for fighting with their iron fists, are haggard when they have the opportunity to come out of the iron gate. Although many of them are skilled in martial arts, they all seem to suffer from anemia. Time really makes people old. According to a friend who has lived there, living in a house like a fly cage, crowded and unable to breathe, is not as good as the bears and tigers in the zoo who occupy a single cage. 丨丨These words may be a bit激, but the facts are not entirely true. The polar bears and Bengal tigers in the zoo, wandering in the iron fence all day long, also seem to have no intention of growing old in this place, but from the perspective of people living in fly cages, it is a bit more comfortable.

The more people in prison, the more sickness increases accordingly. Because there are too many patients, this "universal remedy" was invented under scientific management. According to reports, the name of the new prescription is: "Public Prescription." The name is "public," and the footnote below is probably "everyone can take it." It seems a bit novel to say, but it is not really novel. For example, rich old masters and mistresses should take ginseng, velvet antler, and bird's nest, and young and playful men and women should use "606" and "Her Friend." Prisoners belong to another group of people丨丨Although the reasons for committing crimes are not necessarily the same, under the "common name" of "prisoner," they should naturally take the same medicine. The ingredients of the prescription are unknown, but the prison doctor's hard work is admirable. It is truly a new discovery in the medical field and a great success in scientific management. From then on, it can be simplified and efficient, and it can be done once and for all, and the reward for the medical officer is not small.

But what I want to say is more than this. In this era when the rationalization movement has swept the world, the "universal remedy" in politics seems to be used earlier and more widely. Isn't the soul of Blackshirt leader Mussolini flying from Italy to Germany, to Japan, and to other countries! The humans of the 20th century are smart, and it is even more gratifying that the Chinese are not lagging behind!

The Decline of Peking Opera 281

— Xian

Speaking of Peking Opera, the image of Ryunosuke Akutagawa's "Shanghai Travelogue" immediately pops into my head. He spoke so cheekily. It wasn't because he was our enemy that I already disliked this writer at the time. However, I myself had never stepped through the doors of such theaters, and Peking Opera was foreign to me. I doubted whether the price of one yuan (ordinary) was worth it, and I resented Akutagawa's cheeky remarks in my mind.

The day before yesterday, my uncle came from the countryside and dragged me to accompany him to watch Peking Opera, and I finally obtained my "worth." Of course, I didn't spend that much, but that writer's words were confirmed, although he was a bit too harsh.

Peking Opera has declined, the golden age of "Hong Bi Yuan" and "The Case of the Swapped Crown Prince" is over. A large number of the petty bourgeoisie are intoxicated by the anesthetic of Hollywood. Only when Mei Lanfang, with a doctorate from abroad, comes to Shanghai do the ladies spend money to see this Xiao old man, who claims to have the secret to longevity, dressed as a woman.

I originally doubted that Peking Opera, which foreign gentlemen considered to have artistic meaning, was so depressed in its own country. Is the appreciation ability of foreign gentlemen really so lacking? Their own art—movies—is also heading towards suicide, with sensuality, beast films, air battles, and even gods and monsters, always the same old tired tricks. Without seeking self-improvement, they are accustomed to using speculative methods to cater to low-level interests. How few do not fail!

All the old rules of the Peking Opera world are as unchangeable as the Pamir Mountains. At the entrance stands a "Ah! Two gentlemen!"—the loud voice of the usher. I wonder if Mei Lanfang used this kind of attracting method when performing abroad? We stepped through that self-closing door like visiting guests in the old days. Before eight o'clock, on the corner of the advertising curtain, a group of people were sweating and playing the overture. They were working so hard that an old lady covered her ears and said, "It's giving me a headache!" My head only ached faintly; young people still have this advantage.

On the seats in the first ten rows, the program for today's performance was laid out, and four high-legged pots were arranged in a group, indicating that they had been reserved by the ladies of the consulate(?). We also discounted our one-hundred-point "foreign" value, but I also admitted that my nearsightedness and the old lady's headache were self-inflicted. Can't you cheer from the third floor?

The curtain rises.

This is the Qing Dynasty—I write "Qing Dynasty" directly. I wonder if the Puyi government agrees?—a story of an imperial envoy, which can be endlessly performed like "The Case of the Swapped Crown Prince."

Plot: A lecherous monk picks flowers, a young master falls into misfortune. There is an imperial envoy dressed in the style of the Song Dynasty, a person wearing glasses dressed in Napoleon's attire, Shanghai dialect, Suzhou dialect, and also pidgin English. Interspersed within are battle scenes advocating martial spirit during times of national crisis. Instead of red faces and white faces, there are airplanes and big

Page 20

cannons; as for "dancing" that can "save the country," it is also "all-inclusive." A great masterpiece of 1933, combining slapstick, romance, sensuality, glamour, and war in one pot!

Children clap their hands and say, "It's so good!" The old lady with a headache shakes her head; I didn't ask if the headache was because it wasn't good or not. A girl with red lips said娇声 to a gentleman in a suit, "That dog is so well-behaved, even more so than you!" and poked his nose with her red onion finger painted with rouge.

This is an undeniable fact: that dog is indeed more well-behaved than "people." From their criticism of the dog, it can be known that many people are not watching the play.

Peking Opera has declined. Strive to improve! Since real dogs on stage have produced "human" results, quickly replace the horse whip in "Si Lang Visits His Mother" with a mount.

My head still aches faintly, so I won't say much. This is a free advertisement. Those who want to see the dog perform, might as well spend a "sheep." Come, come, try and see.

Many men are speaking out on behalf of women, rejoicing greatly, while women themselves don't seem to care that much. Since the eastward spread of European and American customs, the personnel and society of our noble country have undergone sudden changes in details and minor branches. Adding a foreign signboard, the most significant change is probably the change in gender relations. In the past (referring to before Westernization), our female compatriots all lived a secluded life like prisoners. Bearing children and managing the household were their only missions, which pressed them down like蒲垫. Of course, this was somewhat wrong. Now, we can finally say that good fortune has arrived. There are women who are county magistrates, and there are also women who are committee members. Extending this to government agencies, companies, and banks, all have female compatriots standing tall and working in society like men. With this one turn, the relationship between men and women becomes extremely strange and complex. Some agree with this, and some oppose it. Some despise it out of jealousy, and some praise it with cheers and songs. Thus, many new nouns have been added, such as female "vases," "queens," "campus belles," "modern ladies," "women of the times," and at the extreme end, "female heroes," "female hooligans," "prostitutes," "salted pork shops," etc. Although their meanings are different, their source is the same—all of them should be attributed to European and American customs.

In fact, in this era, women are indeed awe-inspiring and unapproachable; and the greatness of their magic is something that everyone knows and can talk about. Escape from Annoyance 284

— Bing

This is indeed a kind of annoyance, which needs to be found a way to escape.

The attic that had been empty for a month suddenly had a young couple move in two weeks ago one evening. We live in the front living room, and the so-called attic is built on top of the back living room. Because it is an attic, all four sides are solid, so there is nowhere to set up windows, so there are no windows. There is only one side facing our room, with small wooden squares nailed into many diagonal square openings, more than a丈 wide, but less than two feet high. The air needed in the attic all relies on our room for transportation. Precisely because it is a通洞 partition like a lattice window, the sound is very communicative, even the slight咕咕 in the throat and the sound of swallowing phlegm can be heard clearly, which also planted the seeds for the origin of the annoyance.

From the mouth of the second landlord, I learned that this young couple had just come from the countryside. Looking at their behavior and decorations, it is believable that they are genuine 内地帮. The man leaves early in the morning and does not return until late at night, so I have never recognized him clearly. The impression is very vague. As for the woman, I can sketch a general outline: a face that seems to have been baked ripe by the sun, smeared with a thick layer of snow cream, looks like a crumpled piece of white wax paper. The unevenly developed figure is clothed in a delicate-looking, seemingly modern cheongsam with a floral green梯, which reveals many凸峰 on the body (forgive me for not praising her for having a curvy beauty). The two full breasts in front of her chest are like two strong sole fish, plus a pair of light green纱袜 on her feet, it can be affirmed that she is already a quasi-urban woman who is intoxicated by modernity, about twenty years old.

However, she is, after all, a来路货 who has suffered hardships. She does not have great extravagances. Although squatting in the attic where she can hardly stand upright, she is still complacent, which is, to some extent, due to the enthusiasm and love of the couple.

The laughter of "Eat, eat, eat," mixed with the lewd sound of翻云覆雨, at least two bouts every night, and we, who were sleeping in the front living room below, were disturbed and unable to rest.

"Such a couple, I'm afraid they'll get sick—no restraint at all!" Wu Jun, who was disturbed beyond endurance, often worried about them like this.

"Yes, I didn't expect there to be such people who斵伤生命—but they say that this environment is really not good for us!" I went on to warn ourselves.

"Later, we have to find a way, when they...(please forgive me for replacing it with...) we will狂呌, to see if they still dare to be so放纵!"

"Yes, indeed, we only have this扫兴 plan!"

Unexpectedly, it was not灵騐 at all, which was really annoying. We犯呌, but they became even more狂暴, as if they were deliberately proud and示威 towards us. Therefore, we转舵掉向 and发駡借题, but they just pretended not to understand.

We have been annoyed like this for almost two weeks. I only respect and stay away from them, retreat three舍, and one late night, I went to a friend's house to borrow a night.

The day before yesterday, I came back, and it was said that this pair of hot young couple had moved away, and it was said that they had moved back to the countryside. There were two explanations for the reason of the move. According to the news探来 by Wu Jun, it was like this:

"Because the man got sick and couldn't make a living, so they moved back to the countryside."

According to the second landlord:

"Because the man discovered that the woman was a bit irregular, and had a苟且暧昩 affair with Li Dayou in the back building, so he sent her down to the countryside."

"No matter what the reason for moving away, it's finally relieved our annoyance!" I said with a庆幸透了着.

Clerk Communication

Disaster from the Sky 286

Dear Editor:

I am a female student about to graduate from junior high school.

Page 21

Formally, I seem very fortunate, often with the protection of my parents and the guidance of my teachers; but disaster has struck from the sky, and now a very serious problem has arisen, which may prevent me from living such a comfortable life again, and if it is not handled well, perhaps my family will be disbanded one day.

The matter is like this: My father had a concubine fifteen years ago (she was a prostitute). At that time, my mother strongly opposed it; but because of the opposition, she suffered a lot of abuse and tasted all kinds of oppression and suffering. Now, she (that prostitute) is still working outside as my father's concubine, and my mother! She just pretends not to know, doesn't ask or hear, and they also live in peace. Who knew that last month, my father brought up the old matter again and proposed the idea of bringing her into the house. My mother certainly refused to agree, crying and arguing, and this lasted for a month. Later, after the explanation of many elders and the persuasion of friends, she agreed. However, after entering the house, she still lived outside.

Today, when I came home from school, I saw my mother crying there again; I was shocked and knew that something must have happened. The reason is very simple: this afternoon, my father brought home many ready-made little girl clothes, saying that she (that prostitute) sent them to me, my sister, and my little brother; at that time, my mother thought why she needed to please us, and the two had a quarrel. When my father was leaving, he said that after the Dragon Boat Festival, he would not be responsible for all the expenses of the family.

My father often uses this sentence to intimidate my mother; but this time my father seemed to say it in a serious tone, and I am afraid that there will be a day to implement it. If it is implemented, then what will happen?

If I drop out of school and go to make a living, one person may not have problems; but how can the elderly grandmother, the unfortunate mother, the ignorant young sister, and the young brother who is not yet one year old, as well as a wet nurse and a little maid, support a family of seven! And how difficult is it for a weak woman of seventeen years old to go to the dangerous path of society to make a living? The future is boundless, what kind of occupation is good to find! After thinking about it thousands of times, there is no good way.

Dear Editor: You are the guide of people, the bright light on the dark road. Seeing that you have already solved the problems of many people, please also give me practical guidance on this problem. I wish you

good health! Zhu Xu敬上

××××

Editor's Note: Ms. Zhu's letter seems to want to shoulder the responsibility of maintaining a family of seven: her ambition is commendable, but her actions are not feasible. You are a seventeen-year-old girl who has not graduated from junior high school. I am not afraid that you will get angry and say a word. Your knowledge and experience are still immature. It may be difficult for one person to take care of themselves, so how can they shoulder this family burden? Therefore, this matter should find another way out. You still have to continue your studies, and wait until your knowledge and experience reach a considerable level before considering it.

The art of dealing with the world as a person lies in having a consistent spirit. Be firm to the end, and be gentle to the end. Although it sounds good to be both firm and gentle, if it is not done well, it will often fall into a dilemma. Your mother suffered a loss in this regard regarding the matter of your honorable father taking a concubine. Speaking of firmness, since you had already opposed it, you can always oppose it to the end according to the legal provisions of one husband and one wife. Why did you agree to her entering the house. The law stipulates that those who obtain the consent of the wife shall not be convicted of bigamy. Speaking of gentleness, then after allowing her to enter the house, when she sent clothes, whether it was pleasing ghosts or sincerely wanting to be good, you should not have broken out and抢白.

Now, the matter can still be salvaged. He will never really abandon his old mother, wife, and children because of legal reasons; just give him a way out, I am afraid that he will really have the nerve to ignore the household expenses? However, constant quarrels between families are not a good thing, so I hope that Ms. Zhu will persuade her mother to think about it. Now that things have become a reality, you can only use the means of gentleness to overcome firmness.

Novel

The Life of the Five Concubines (10) (1) (Continued) 288

— Ling He

The night was already deep, and Master Zhang was sleeping beside her again. This evening, Master Zhang was very興旧, he not only told her that he had recently運動 his superiors with 15,000 yuan, and would be dispatched to take office immediately, but also said that he would marry her back, and in the future, she would have children, and after the death of the first wife, she would inevitably be promoted. She had heard such words from his mouth dozens of times, and it was inevitably troublesome to say them again and again, but today they also made sense; it was easier to be蹂躪 to death by one man than to serve many men at the same time, right? As for whether she would be promoted in the future, there was no need to worry about it. So:

"Okay, I'll marry him."

This妖精, but because she had no hope of having a son, she had to allow it; now that the old ghost was dead, a寡婊子 would certainly not be able to give birth to a drop of blood, and Master Zhang had said such words when he was dying, so Miss Liu could not be considered Master Zhang's姨太太.

The bank deposit book in her hand was taken back by the housekeeper on the third day after the old man's death. In addition to allowing her to keep the gold and silver jewelry as souvenirs, she was also given 1,200 yuan as maintenance expenses. Before finding someone, she was allowed to continue living in this building: in this way, the first wife's character was also very generous.

But Liu Gu was not concerned about these, 　silver money and property, she had never had a good plan for. However, she always had to live on, and this point did not seem to be a problem, so how should she live on? She still had a good plan for this. So this question lingered in her mind for several days, but she could only be aware of a few points, which were: 丨

"I am a widow now. But it's not surprising, probably a罚 woman can't avoid being a widow...

"Am I going to marry someone else? Am I still going to be someone else's嬝太太? No...

"Hum, am I still 'falling in happiness' now? Oh 　Could it be that 　I'm still dreaming?

"No, I am my own person now. I am my own person now!"

Movie Special

A Visit to the Kamata Photography Studio in Japan 289

— Donglin

What I Saw One Morning Four Years Ago

In my previously published "Japanese Film屑 Talk," I once said that this Kamata Photography Studio is the place where Shochiku Eiga Co., Ltd. specializes in taking modern films. In Japan, it is the oldest and best modern film photography studio.

This was one summer morning four years ago, right? At that time, I was still living in Omori, outside Tokyo. I got the news that the Kamata Photography Studio was open, and I quickly took the elevated train to Kamata. It was only one stop from Omori to Kamata, so in less than five minutes, I had reached my destination. Walking out of the Kamata train station, going north, and turning a bay, I saw the photography studio surrounded by red and white cloth in the distance.

After buying a ticket, I ran into a large house, where there were many long tables, on which were displayed countless models of buildings and vehicles. I asked the receptionist standing next to me, what are these used for? He said to me that these are the various houses and mansions reflected on the screen, and the fire scene is to burn these models. I listened to his words, half believing and half doubting, and left.

Walking out of the back door of this large house, just as I was about to move forward, my hat was blown more than a丈 away by the wind. I couldn't help but be surprised:: how can there be such a big wind in such good weather? I picked up my hat, and my curiosity led me to go over and see what was causing the trouble there. Turning a corner, I understood; it turned out that the wind was coming from a tall and large thing, like a fan. The engineer standing next to it was explaining to the audience that this machine was used to make狂风.

Leaving the crowd, I turned another corner and saw a small train station; there was a wooden train front in the station, installed in the appearance of parking. I thought this was the so-called train in the movie! Walking less than a few steps, there was a small pond in front, and the flowers and plants on all sides were cultivated like a garden. There are only a few steps away from a train station and a garden. This kind of scene cannot be seen anywhere other than a photography studio.

There were many people surrounded in front, so I also walked up, squeezed into the crowd, and saw clearly. It turned out that they were taking the scene of rain. Speaking of this rain, it was really ridiculous. This was just the water that people standing high up were撥 down! An actor, also without holding an umbrella, was戰慓ing like a "river ghost" being撥 by the water. I couldn't help but think of the hardships of being a movie actor.

Looking around like this, it was noon before I knew it. I was very hungry, so I went out to eat lunch.

Movie Review

Review of "Peach Blossom Village" Happy Ever After 290

— Ling He

Following "Tell Me Tonight" (Spring River Flower Moon Night), we now have this "Happy Ever After" with the same sentiment. This is, of course, not accidental. We can find the producer's intention to some extent in this. Everyone knows what the content of the previous film was, so there seems to be no need to dissect it here. So what does "Peach Blossom Village" tell us? It ridicules Hollywood producers and exposes young girls' fantasies about glamorous movies. However, these are not the main tasks of the film's creators. Its most important purpose is to teach the audience to escape reality in front of beautiful pictures and retreat to a utopia for the sake of perfect love. Obviously, in today's society, the idyllic life has long been destroyed by the realistic economic system, and we are no longer obedient people in a prosperous age. We struggle day and night. Is there any possibility for us to "return to Peach Blossom Village to live a leisurely life"? However, this is precisely the author's intention: to teach us to continue to fantasize in fantasy.

As mentioned above, in order to make the audience indulge in a beautiful illusion, there must be beautiful pictures. Therefore, the director must use skillful techniques to fill the film with romantic sentiments through singing and dancing, and add exquisite photography to enhance the intoxicating color, so that his mission can be accomplished.

However, the director is still not very lively in a few scenes. The most obvious is that Lilian Harvey is in the middle, with a male on each side, lined up and repeated, for several shots. This is inevitably too mechanical on the screen. Secondly, the director's sentiment is not soft enough, if "softness" is to be the essence of this film.

At the same time, there is no clear climax in the play, and no strong stimulation at all. Although these may not be necessary in the play, it cannot give the audience any impression. As far as the director is concerned, no characteristics can be found.

In terms of actors, no one has achieved amazing results, and they are all lazy and mediocre. The scene where the heroine Lilian Harvey dances in her dream and in front of the American producers reminds us of her past achievements, and she can still maintain that lively attitude in other aspects. Jack Hulbert and Sonnie Hale are not seen in this film, but there are also very few chaotic scenes.

The sound is good, and the scenery is also good. However, the best is the photography. However, no matter what, in terms of skill, it is indeed a film worth seeing.

Little Fairbanks 291

— Fu Lun

Will Tour China

After Little Fairbanks divorced his wife Joan Crawford, he was suddenly accused of seduction. Fairbanks is resorting to legal solutions. (After this case is closed, he will pack his bags and travel west, where he will meet his father, Fairbanks, in Shanghai, and then go hunting in various places together. It is estimated that it will have to wait until the autumn is cool, because the lawsuit still needs to be delayed for some time. In addition, Little Fairbanks and Joan Crawford still visit each other from time to time after announcing their separation. According to Fairbanks himself, their relationship is closer than before, and they have gone out together four times, which is more enjoyable than traveling with any other woman. As for the divorce, he and Joan are unwilling to discuss it immediately, because neither of them intends to marry again. Little Fairbanks has vowed to wait until he has achieved success before talking about marrying again.

(Audience Opinions: Impressions of "Rouge Market") 292

— Shi Zeyong

Following "Flower of Freedom," the Star Motion Picture Company's "Rouge Market," a Four Seas Tong sound film, was released at the New Light Grand Theatre on the 14th! At first glance at the naming of these four words, we feel that this evil society, with the strong rouge color of Shanghai, can know the status of women in society, but only like this!

In Shanghai in the 20th century, the occupations of general women do not have a stable status at all; although they are shouting slogans of women's liberation, freedom, and improvement every day, which one has a thorough understanding? Even if they are as determined as Li Cuifen, they will inevitably be insulted and played with by capitalists. What about some women who are willing to degenerate?

Here, I do not intend to offend modern women; indeed, their will is too weak! And they don't understand the hypocrisy of modern society at all. They only rely on a moment of impulse, like "moths to a flame," rushing towards the place with light, forgetting the danger of the future, to seek a bright way out from the dark society, and they have to endure hardship to have good results. Otherwise, it's not that easy!

A Few Thoughts After Watching "Rouge Market" 293

— Mei Cun

"Rouge Market" is indeed a film with a better consciousness. It exposes the evil forces in society and the darkness between men and women, which makes me feel satisfied after watching it. The following are my thoughts after watching it:

First, there are no trams or cars around the department store, and even rickshaws are only one or two, and there are few pedestrians coming and going. I think that since it is called a department store, it should be located in a lively place like Wing On or Sincere, so that it can be suitable for the prosperity of a large company.

Second, the scene inside the company should also be decorated more lively. For example, there are only elevators that go in and no elevators that go out, and there are only four or five, which seems too bland.

Third, it is also inappropriate for customers to flirt with female clerks when buying things in the rouge department, and for the female clerks to flirt with them. I think the audience is dissatisfied with this point. Several friends sitting next to me were saying, "There is simply no such thing."

Fourth, Hu Die, who plays Li Cuifen, has excellent facial expressions, especially when she is thinking silently, her pupils flash, and her worries are fully revealed. If she had used other people's voices to explain her meaning at that time, it would have been more powerful.

Fifth, the last few scenes show the results of the struggle, from picking tea leaves to answering the phone and opening a small shop. The introduction of several sections of life is very simple, which is the director's cleverness.

My Review of "Rouge Market" 294

— Xu Qiong

The Insertion of Love is Unreasonable

Women's occupation is indeed a serious problem in our current China. It is not harsh to say that general companies, banks, and stores recruit female employees, and the beautiful name is to promote women's occupation, but in fact? It's just to attract general, lustful people. Therefore, many insulting nicknames for women have come: what vases, screens, and living signs, instinctively tell us: women's occupation in China is just playing around. If you are not coquettish and charming, you cannot attract customers, and if you do not show loyalty to your superiors, you cannot keep your job. This is the golden rule of women's occupation. "Rouge Market" grasped this realistic women's issue to expose it, although it is very appropriate; but we believe that the exposure is not enough, and an unreasonable placement of a distorted love story shook the entire play itself and blurred the audience's mind!

In the ending, it is too full of Romance, because it will not be so rapid and successful to struggle out of work. The old wolf mother, so-called to recognize the shortcomings of society, also has not recognized at all.

As for the expression: too contrived, it is possible for female employees to hum and sing, but it is too much to dance in the counter; the young manager's rubbing his eyes to look at female employees is too contrived; Hu Die's several crying scenes are very good; Wang Xianzhai is successful.

Movie Novel Eternal Regret (The White Sister) (2) 295

— Si Ping

Starring Helen Hayes, produced by MGM

Sacrificing Reputation and Happiness for Love

Ernest started chatting again, but another twist came. An old car, turning and twisting through the crowd, crashed violently into the back of the prince's car. Angela looked anxiously out the back window, her father and the driver scurrying off to investigate how badly the car was damaged.

The person who came out of this old car was wearing a military uniform! A soldier, Angela thought, was beautiful. The man, glimpsing her curious gaze, ran to the car.

"Good morning," he said, with a charming smile. But Ernest pulled down the window curtain at the sight of this expression. "Shameless!" he grumbled, with an aristocratic temper. The car then started moving.

"Who was that?" the young soldier asked his laughing companions as he ran back to his car.

"That, Giovanni, is old Prince Sheremende," one person said. "And that beautiful princess is his daughter."

Giovanni patted the engine of his dilapidated car as if he had found a treasure. His heart had already floated away, following the charming smile of the beautiful shadow carried by the gorgeous car.

At the Sheremende Palace, Ernest, adhering to the details, kissed Angela's hand and said with a smile that he was rushing to catch a train to Rome. Angela scurried to the window facing the town, leaning out in quiet reverie.

"They are so happy, Mina," she said. "Listen to that music!" She slightly lifted her skirt and tried a dance step.

"Mina, I dreamed of him again," she said, blushing.

"Who is he?" Mina asked, doing needlework.

"The person I dreamed of. This time his name was Wolanski. He was riding a white horse with black spots. Mother was there too. She was very beautiful! Golden hair. Does Mother have golden hair? Why are there no photos of Mother?"

This was not a new question, but Mina replied:

"I told you! Because your father doesn't want it." Angela returned to the balcony, leaned on the railing, and gazed intently.

"Mina," she said suddenly, "let's go out! Is it still two o'clock for us to eat? Let's go see the carnival!" Angela said, rushing into the room, grabbing her shawl. "I'll go alone," she resisted, said, and ran away. Mina said, "You can't!" and grabbed his coat and hurried to catch up.

It's really lively to see the carnival up close! Her heart was pounding. Farmers mixed with soldiers, dancing, playing, and the front of the parade had characters from unofficial history, giants, and monsters made up of two or three people. A horse, with its nose stretched out, sniffed at the extremely happy Angela, and suddenly fell to the ground, rolling over and over. At this moment, the soldier from the old car appeared in the crowd, standing in front of them, bending slightly.

"Good afternoon, Princess," Giovanni said. This time, there was no stern hand to pull down the curtain between him and that charming, blushing face.
